The Condition for Creative Power: Response to an Objection
Nasafi answers an objection about the condition for human creative power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the possibility of a condition does not guarantee the possibility of the conditioned, particularly in the context of human creative power.

Core Idea
A possible condition does not make the conditioned possible if it is independently impossible.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi addresses a key objection from those who argue that human creative power must be possible because its condition (knowledge) is possible. He explains why this reasoning is flawed and shifts the discussion back to the actual dispute. The passage highlights a subtle logical distinction crucial for understanding the Maturidi position on human agency.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the first sentence of the passage carefully. The opponents claim that since knowledge (the condition) is possible, power (the conditioned) must also be possible.
Notice that they argue from possibility of condition to possibility of conditioned.
2
Nasafi's first response: deviation from the dispute
Nasafi points out that this objection shifts the topic. The real dispute is about actions that occur without knowledge, not about actions where knowledge is present.
The opponents are mixing two different scenarios.
3
Key arguments against the objection
Nasafi presents two points: (1) Humans cannot conceptualize bringing something from non-existence, so the condition for creative power is inconceivable. (2) Even if the condition were possible, the conditioned may be prevented by another proof.
The second point is crucial: possibility of condition does not guarantee possibility of conditioned.
4
Logical clarification and conclusion
Nasafi explains that the impossibility of the dependent requires the absence of its condition, not the impossibility of the condition itself. The opponents are thus deviating from the core issue.
This clarifies that the condition itself may be possible, but if it is absent, the dependent cannot exist.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا: من الجائزات ثبوت العلم للعبد بفعله من هذه الوجوه، وإذا كان ثبوت الشرط من الجائزات كان ثبوت القدرة من الجائزات.
قيل لهم هذا عدول عن الكلام في المتنازع ، فإن المتنازع بيننا وبينكم وقع في هذه الأفعال الحاصلة مع الجهل من العباد بها بهذه الوجوه، فادعيتم(٢) أنتم كونها مخلوقة للعباد، ونحن أثبنا ذلك وثبتنا بالدليل استحالته بحمد الله تعالى.
فبعد ذلك تصور ثبوت هذه الشريطة في الجملة مما لا ينفعكم، على أنا نقول: ليس في مقدور البشر الاطلاع على الإخراج من العدم إلى الوجود فلا يتصور شريطة قدرة التخليق، على أن ثبوت شريطة الشيء مما لا يوجب ثبوته إذا امتنع ثبوته بدليل آخر، وقد امتنع هاهنا بدليل آخر، نبين ذلك إذا انتهينا إلى إقامة الدليل على أن إثبات قدرة التخليق تؤدي إلى المحال ، ونحن (۱) نتكلم معكم في حال انعدام العلم (1) الذي هو شريطة ثبوت القدرة فندعي استحالة ثبوتها في حال انعدام العلم الذي هو) شريطة ثبوتها وامتناع ما تعلق ثبوته بوجود شرط يكون ثابتا عند انعدام الشرط، ولا يفتقر امتناع المعلق إلى امتناع الشرط بل يفتقر إلى انعدامه، لأن شرط وجود المعلق وجود نفس الشرط لا إمكان وجوده ، وإذا عرف هذا تبين حيد الخصوم عن محز السؤال (٤) باشتغالهم بمثل هذا الخيال، والله الموفق.
If they say: 'Among possible things is the establishment of knowledge for the servant of his action in these respects, and if the establishment of the condition is among possible things, then the establishment of power is among possible things.' It is said to them: This is a departure from discussing what is disputed. For the dispute between us and you occurred concerning these actions that occur with ignorance on the part of the servants in these respects. You claim that they are created by the servants, and we have proven and established by proof its impossibility, thanks to God. So after that, the conceptualization of the establishment of this condition in general does not benefit you. Furthermore, we say: It is not within human capacity to know how to bring [something] from non-existence into existence, so the condition for the power of creation cannot be conceptualized. Moreover, the establishment of the condition of something does not necessitate its establishment if its establishment is prevented by another proof, and it is prevented here by another proof. We will explain that when we come to present the proof that affirming creative power leads to absurdity. And we are speaking with you in the case of the absence of knowledge, which is the condition for the establishment of power, so we claim the impossibility of its establishment in the case of the absence of knowledge, which is its condition, and the impossibility of what is dependent on a condition that would be fixed when the condition is absent. The impossibility of the dependent does not require the impossibility of the condition but rather requires its absence, because the condition for the existence of the dependent is the existence of the condition itself, not the possibility of its existence. And when this is known, the opponents' deviation from the mark of the question becomes clear by their preoccupation with such fantasy. And God is the granter of success.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer set. The opponents argue that since it is possible for the servant to know his own action (as a condition for power), and if the condition is possible, then the power itself must be possible. Nasafi replies that this shifts the topic: the dispute is about actions that occur without the servant's knowledge, so the opponent cannot appeal to cases where knowledge is present. He then makes several points: first, even if the condition were possible in theory, it does not help the opponent because human beings cannot conceptualize the bringing forth from non-existence; second, the possibility of a condition does not entail the possibility of the conditioned if there is another proof against it; third, they are specifically discussing the case when knowledge (the condition) is absent, so they claim that power is impossible when its condition is absent; fourth, the impossibility of a dependent thing requires only the absence of its condition, not the impossibility of the condition itself. Therefore, the opponents are deviating from the core issue by indulging in irrelevant fantasies.

الجائزات

المعلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If a condition is possible, then the conditioned thing must also be possible.
Correction: Nasafi shows that the conditioned can be impossible due to other proofs, even if the condition is possible. Moreover, the impossibility of the conditioned requires only the absence of the condition, not its impossibility.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, why does the possibility of the condition not necessitate the possibility of the conditioned?
A) Because the condition might be impossible in reality
B) Because the conditioned might be prevented by another proof
C) Because the condition is only conceptual
D) Because the opponent is ignorant

Key Takeaway
The possibility of a condition does not guarantee the possibility of the conditioned; the latter may be impossible due to another proof, or simply absent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a time when you felt fully in control of your actions, confident that your knowledge and power were sufficient. After learning that even the condition for creative power is beyond human capacity, how will you cultivate a daily awareness that every successful action is a gift from Allah? Write one practical step you will take.
?
This lesson reveals that the opponents engaged in 'fantasy' by avoiding the core issue of human dependence on Allah. Where in your own life do you avoid uncomfortable truths about your limitations by focusing on irrelevant debates or distractions? Commit to one specific area where you will stop rationalizing and instead submit to the reality of Allah's exclusive creative power.
?
Nasafi emphasizes that the impossibility of the conditioned (your power) requires only the absence of its condition, not the impossibility of the condition. Does this logic expose any false sense of security you hold—like assuming that because you have knowledge or ability in some area, you are guaranteed to produce good results? How will you guard against presumption and instead rely on Allah for the actual existence of conditions?

The Dilemma: God's Freedom or Compulsion in Creating Evil
The author presents a dilemma with two impossible horns.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two impossible consequences that follow from the Mu'tazili claim that God creates the evil aspect of human acts.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazili position forces an impossible choice between evil without evilness and subjecting God to compulsion.

The author begins by forcing a dilemma on the Mu'tazila. If God creates the evil attribute of an act, then either He does so voluntarily or under compulsion. Both options lead to impossibility, as the author demonstrates. This lesson unpacks that dilemma.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text carefully. Notice the structure of conditional statements.
The passage begins with 'law... lazalama' (if... then).
2
Identify the two horns
Locate the two possibilities: God is free (mukhtar) or compelled (mudtar).
The author presents them as 'imma... aw' (either... or).
3
Understand why each is impossible
If God is free, He could refrain, so evil would exist without evilness. If compelled, God is subjected to the servant's power, which is unbelief.
The second horn is called kufr (unbelief) explicitly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على أنا نلزمكم فنقول : لو كان العبد أوجده من حيث إنه فعل والله تعالى أوجده من حيث إنه قبح كما تزعمون للزم أحد أمرين كل واحد منهما محال. وبيانه أن العبد إذا قصد تحصيل الكفر فأوجده إما أن يكون الله تعالى مختارًا من إيجاده من حيث إنه قبح أو مضطر إلى ذلك؟ فإن قالوا: هو مختار نقول : كأن من الجائز أن يمتنع عن إيجاده من حيث إنه قبح فيوجد الكفر بدون صفة القبح وهو محال. وإن قالوا: هو مضطر في إيجاده فهو كفر لما فيه من دعوى المعجز على الله تعالى وإدخاله تحت قدرة الغير وقهره. ولا يلزمنا هذا في التخليق والانتساب على ما قررنا في شبهة الخصوم، لأن كل فعل في ذاته يوصف الله تعالى بالقدرة على الانفراد والاستبداد، والعبد لا يوصف بذلك، إلا أن الله تعالى أجرى العادة أنه يخلق كل فعل قصد العبد اكتسابه. ونفرض الكلام في حركة معينة فنقول : هي قبيل وجودها علمها الله تعالى قدرة إيجادها لو أراد إيجادها على سبيل الاستبداد، والعبد لا يقدر على اكتسابها ومباشرتها بدون إيجاد الله تعالى. ولا يقال لو أراد الله إيجادها فعلاً للعبد مع امتناع العبد عن ذلك هل يحصل ذلك؟ فإن حصل فقد لزم القول باضطرار العبد إذ الفعل الضروري هو الذي يوجد والذي قصد العبد الامتناع عنه، وإن لم يحصل فقد لزم القول بتعجيز الباري جل وعلا، لأنا نقول : لا يتصور عندنا أن يريدها فعلاً للعبد إلا وأن يريد العبد وجود قدرته عليها لاستحالة وجود الفعل الاختياري بلا قدرة ولا يتصور وجود القدرة بدون الفعل فيستحيل إرادة الله إياها أن تكون فعلاً للعبد مع إرادة العبد الامتناع عنها إذ إرادة الامتناع لن تتصور بدون قدرة الامتناع، وقدرة الامتناع يستحيل وجودها بدون نفس الامتناع على ما مر في مسألة الاستطاعة. فأما الإلزام على المعتزلة على الوجه الذي بينا فثابت مقرر، وبالله المعونة والتوفيق.
We say: We hold you to a necessary conclusion: If the servant produced it insofar as it is an act, and God Most High produced it insofar as it is evil, as you claim, then one of two things would necessarily follow, each of which is impossible. Its explanation is that if the servant intends to produce unbelief and produces it, then either God Most High is free in producing it insofar as it is evil, or He is compelled to that? If they say: He is free, we say: It would then be possible for Him to refrain from producing it insofar as it is evil, so unbelief would exist without the attribute of evil, which is impossible. And if they say: He is compelled in producing it, then that is unbelief because it involves claiming incapacity (mu'jiz) for God Most High and subjecting Him to the power and coercion of another. This does not necessarily apply to us concerning creation (takhliq) and attribution (intisab), as we have established in the objection of the opponents, because every act in itself is described by God Most High as having the power of independence and absolute disposal, and the servant is not described with that, except that God Most High has established the custom that He creates every act that the servant intends to acquire. And we suppose the discussion concerning a specific movement and say: Before its existence, God Most High knew that He has the power to create it if He wanted to create it in the manner of absolute disposal, and the servant has no power to acquire it and perform it without God's creation. And it cannot be said: If God wanted to create it as an act of the servant while the servant refrains from it, would that occur? If it occurred, then the statement of the servant's compulsion would necessarily follow, for the compelled act is that which exists while the servant intended to refrain from it; and if it did not occur, then the statement of incapacitating the Exalted and Majestic would necessarily follow. We say: In our view, it is inconceivable that He wants it as an act of the servant unless the servant wants the existence of his power over it, because the existence of a voluntary act without power is impossible, and the existence of power without the act is inconceivable. Therefore, it is impossible that God's wanting it to be an act of the servant occurs together with the servant's intending to refrain from it, because the intention to refrain cannot be conceived without the power to refrain, and the power to refrain cannot exist without the act of refraining itself, as has passed in the issue of capacity (istita'a). As for the necessary conclusion against the Mu'tazila in the manner we have explained, it is established and confirmed, and with God is aid and success.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazili claim that regarding human acts, God creates the act insofar as it is evil while the servant creates it insofar as it is an act. The author first forces a dilemma: If God creates the evil aspect, either He does so voluntarily or under compulsion. If voluntarily, then He could refrain, leading to evil existing without the attribute of evil (impossible). If under compulsion, then God is subject to the servant's power, which is unbelief. The author then distinguishes his own position: For every act, God has independent power to create it, and the servant acquires it by God's custom. He elaborates on a specific example of a movement, explaining that God could create it independently, but the servant cannot acquire it without God's creation. He then addresses a hypothetical: if God wanted to create it as the servant's act while the servant refrains, it is impossible because the servant's voluntary act requires his power, and power requires the act; thus, the scenario is inconceivable. The argument concludes that the Mu'tazili view is refuted.

الكفر
المعجز
الاضطرار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: It is possible for God to create the evil attribute of an act while the servant creates the act itself.
Correction: This leads to two impossible consequences: either evil without evilness or God subject to compulsion.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what follows if God is free in creating the evil aspect?
A) Unbelief would exist without the attribute of evil.
B) God would be subject to the servant's power.
C) The act would be good.
D) The servant would be the sole creator.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazili claim forces an impossible choice: either God can refrain from creating evil (making evil impossible) or He is compelled (making Him subject to creation).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a sin, do you ever feel that God 'made you do it'? If so, where does that leave your own responsibility? This dilemma shows that such a thought leads either to absurdity or blasphemy—which one is closer to your own heart?
?
The Mu'tazila tried to protect God's justice by separating His role in evil. But this argument shows that any separation leads to an impossible choice. Are you willing to accept that God creates all things, including your evil actions, without compromising His justice or your accountability? How does your daily repentance reflect that belief?
?
If God were compelled to create evil, that would be unbelief. But do you sometimes live as if God is compelled—complaining about your circumstances as if He had no choice but to give them to you? What would it mean to truly believe that He is free and just in everything He creates?

The Author's Position and the Hypothetical Example
The author distinguishes his own view and defends it with a hypothetical example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's own view on divine creation and human acquisition, and why the Mu'tazili objection fails.

Core Idea
God has independent power to create every act, while the servant acquires it by God's custom.

After exposing the dilemma, the author clarifies his own position to show why the Mu'tazili objection does not apply. He explains that God has absolute power over all acts, and the servant only acquires them by God's established custom. This is illustrated with a detailed example involving a specific movement.

Guided Path
1
Read the author's distinction
Pay attention to the terms 'takhliq' (creation) and 'intisab' (attribution).
The author says the Mu'tazili objection does not apply to his view.
2
Understand the example of a movement
The author supposes a specific movement and discusses God's power versus the servant's power.
Notice that God's power is absolute (istibdad) while the servant's power is limited.
3
Follow the hypothetical objection and reply
The author considers: if God wants to create the act as the servant's act while the servant refrains, what happens? He shows both outcomes are impossible, concluding the scenario is inconceivable.
This demonstrates the harmony between divine creation and human acquisition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على أنا نلزمكم فنقول : لو كان العبد أوجده من حيث إنه فعل والله تعالى أوجده من حيث إنه قبح كما تزعمون للزم أحد أمرين كل واحد منهما محال. وبيانه أن العبد إذا قصد تحصيل الكفر فأوجده إما أن يكون الله تعالى مختارًا من إيجاده من حيث إنه قبح أو مضطر إلى ذلك؟ فإن قالوا: هو مختار نقول : كأن من الجائز أن يمتنع عن إيجاده من حيث إنه قبح فيوجد الكفر بدون صفة القبح وهو محال. وإن قالوا: هو مضطر في إيجاده فهو كفر لما فيه من دعوى المعجز على الله تعالى وإدخاله تحت قدرة الغير وقهره. ولا يلزمنا هذا في التخليق والانتساب على ما قررنا في شبهة الخصوم، لأن كل فعل في ذاته يوصف الله تعالى بالقدرة على الانفراد والاستبداد، والعبد لا يوصف بذلك، إلا أن الله تعالى أجرى العادة أنه يخلق كل فعل قصد العبد اكتسابه. ونفرض الكلام في حركة معينة فنقول : هي قبيل وجودها علمها الله تعالى قدرة إيجادها لو أراد إيجادها على سبيل الاستبداد، والعبد لا يقدر على اكتسابها ومباشرتها بدون إيجاد الله تعالى. ولا يقال لو أراد الله إيجادها فعلاً للعبد مع امتناع العبد عن ذلك هل يحصل ذلك؟ فإن حصل فقد لزم القول باضطرار العبد إذ الفعل الضروري هو الذي يوجد والذي قصد العبد الامتناع عنه، وإن لم يحصل فقد لزم القول بتعجيز الباري جل وعلا، لأنا نقول : لا يتصور عندنا أن يريدها فعلاً للعبد إلا وأن يريد العبد وجود قدرته عليها لاستحالة وجود الفعل الاختياري بلا قدرة ولا يتصور وجود القدرة بدون الفعل فيستحيل إرادة الله إياها أن تكون فعلاً للعبد مع إرادة العبد الامتناع عنها إذ إرادة الامتناع لن تتصور بدون قدرة الامتناع، وقدرة الامتناع يستحيل وجودها بدون نفس الامتناع على ما مر في مسألة الاستطاعة. فأما الإلزام على المعتزلة على الوجه الذي بينا فثابت مقرر، وبالله المعونة والتوفيق.
We say: We hold you to a necessary conclusion: If the servant produced it insofar as it is an act, and God Most High produced it insofar as it is evil, as you claim, then one of two things would necessarily follow, each of which is impossible. Its explanation is that if the servant intends to produce unbelief and produces it, then either God Most High is free in producing it insofar as it is evil, or He is compelled to that? If they say: He is free, we say: It would then be possible for Him to refrain from producing it insofar as it is evil, so unbelief would exist without the attribute of evil, which is impossible. And if they say: He is compelled in producing it, then that is unbelief because it involves claiming incapacity (mu'jiz) for God Most High and subjecting Him to the power and coercion of another. This does not necessarily apply to us concerning creation (takhliq) and attribution (intisab), as we have established in the objection of the opponents, because every act in itself is described by God Most High as having the power of independence and absolute disposal, and the servant is not described with that, except that God Most High has established the custom that He creates every act that the servant intends to acquire. And we suppose the discussion concerning a specific movement and say: Before its existence, God Most High knew that He has the power to create it if He wanted to create it in the manner of absolute disposal, and the servant has no power to acquire it and perform it without God's creation. And it cannot be said: If God wanted to create it as an act of the servant while the servant refrains from it, would that occur? If it occurred, then the statement of the servant's compulsion would necessarily follow, for the compelled act is that which exists while the servant intended to refrain from it; and if it did not occur, then the statement of incapacitating the Exalted and Majestic would necessarily follow. We say: In our view, it is inconceivable that He wants it as an act of the servant unless the servant wants the existence of his power over it, because the existence of a voluntary act without power is impossible, and the existence of power without the act is inconceivable. Therefore, it is impossible that God's wanting it to be an act of the servant occurs together with the servant's intending to refrain from it, because the intention to refrain cannot be conceived without the power to refrain, and the power to refrain cannot exist without the act of refraining itself, as has passed in the issue of capacity (istita'a). As for the necessary conclusion against the Mu'tazila in the manner we have explained, it is established and confirmed, and with God is aid and success.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazili claim that regarding human acts, God creates the act insofar as it is evil while the servant creates it insofar as it is an act. The author first forces a dilemma: If God creates the evil aspect, either He does so voluntarily or under compulsion. If voluntarily, then He could refrain, leading to evil existing without the attribute of evil (impossible). If under compulsion, then God is subject to the servant's power, which is unbelief. The author then distinguishes his own position: For every act, God has independent power to create it, and the servant acquires it by God's custom. He elaborates on a specific example of a movement, explaining that God could create it independently, but the servant cannot acquire it without God's creation. He then addresses a hypothetical: if God wanted to create it as the servant's act while the servant refrains, it is impossible because the servant's voluntary act requires his power, and power requires the act; thus, the scenario is inconceivable. The argument concludes that the Mu'tazili view is refuted.

Key Terms
التخليق
الانتساب
الاستطاعة
الاضطرار
المعجز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The author's view implies that God compels human actions, leaving no room for human responsibility.
Correction: The author shows that human intention and power are necessary for voluntary acts; God's creation does not negate the servant's role but rather enables it through custom.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what makes it impossible for God to create an act as the servant's act while the servant intends to refrain?
A) God lacks the power to do so.
B) The servant's intention to refrain requires the power to refrain, which cannot exist without the act of refraining.
C) The act would be created without any agent.
D) The servant would be forced, contradicting free will.

Key Takeaway
God's independent power and the servant's acquisition are compatible; the Mu'tazili objection fails because it overlooks the necessary connection between intention, power, and act.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly acknowledge that every good deed you perform is created by God's power alone? How does this realization change your gratitude and reliance on Him for even your smallest acts of obedience?
?
When you fall into sin, do you immediately blame God's decree, or do you recognize your own acquisition (intention and power) in that act? How can the author's argument push you to take full responsibility for your choices while still trusting God's sovereignty?
?
If you knew that your ability to pray, give charity, or control your anger is entirely a gift from God created at that moment, would you prepare differently for each act of worship? What specific step will you take today to ask God for the power to act before you act?

The Dilemma of Two Agents Creating the Same Act
Author presents a dilemma on shared creative power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical dilemma that arises if both God and the servant are said to have creative power over the same act, and why it leads to incapacitating God.

Core Idea
If the servant creates, God either creates the same act again (impossible) or loses power (incapacitation).

The author lays out a critical division: either a single act falls under the power of two agents (which is considered possible in itself) or each agent creates independently. He then examines the latter scenario and poses a powerful dilemma that exposes the theological impossibility of affirming creative power (takhlīq) for the servant. This lesson walks you through that dilemma and its conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Understand the division
Read the opening lines where the author states the two possibilities regarding a single act and two agents. Notice he says the first is among the possibilities, but he pauses to examine it due to necessity.
The passage begins with a reference to a previous chapter.
2
Identify the dilemma
Focus on the conditional: if the servant brings the act into existence, what happens to God's power over that act? The author presents two options and explains why each is impossible.
Option 1: God still has power → creating what exists. Option 2: God loses power → servant incapacitated God.
3
Grasp the conclusion
The author concludes that both options are impossible, so affirming creative power for the servant necessarily leads to incapacitation of God (ta'jiz), which is absurd.
This conclusion is central to the Maturidi position on kasb (acquisition) versus creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا القسم يليق بالفصل الثالث وهو أن دخول مقدور واحد تحت قدرة قادرين من جملة المجوزات، وإنما وقفنا فيه في هذا الفعل لضرورة التقسيم وإذا بطل هذا القسم تعين القسم الآخر وهو أن الله تعالى عليه قدرة كما أن للعبد عليه قدرة، وينفرد كل واحد بإيجاده كما ذهب إليه طائفة منهم.
ثم على هذا القسم نلزم فنقول : إذا أوجد العبد هل بقى الله تعالى على ذلك الفعل قدرة الإيجاد ؟ فإن قالوا: نعم، فقد أحالوا ، لأن إيجاد الموجود محل. وإن قالوا: لا، فقد أقروا بإزالة العبد قدرة الله تعالى عما كانت ثابتة عليه ومنعه إياه عن إيجاد ما كان قادرا على إيجاده، وهذا هو التعجيز عندنا والمنع عندكم، وكل ذلك محال ممتنع، والله الموفق.
العبد.
فإن قالوا: يوجده الله تعالى في الحالة الثانية من حالة وجوده الذي أوجده
قيل: الإلزام في الحالة الأولى باق ولا اعتراض لكم عليه، ثم إيجاده أيضا في الحالة الثانية مستحيل، فإن ما أوجده العبد عندنا مستحيل البقاء وعندكم على اختلاف فيما بينكم قد يكون مما يبقى وقد يكون مما لا يبقى - فإن كان مما لا يبقى فإيجاده في الثاني مستحيل، لأنه يصير باقيًا لوجوده في الوقتين المتواليين اللذين لا يتصور العدم فيهما بينهما، وهذا هو حد البقاء والقول ببقاء ما لا يبقى محال، وإن كان مما يبقى فهو في الثاني من زمان وجوده موجود وإيجاد الموجود محال. وعرف بهذه الفصول : أن القول بإثبات قدرة التخليق للعبد يؤدي إلى تعجيز الله تعالى، وهو محال
وإنما قلنا: إنه يؤدي إلى إبطال دلائل الموحدين، لأنه يؤدي إلى تعجيز الباري على ما بينا، ولو جاز أن يكون الباري جل وعلا عاجزا بتعجيز الغير إياه ولا تبطل ربوبيته لجاز أن يكون للعالم صانعان وأكثر ، وإن كان البعض يعجز بعضا، وقد قررنا هذا الفصل على الاستقصاء في مسألة إثبات وحدانية القديم جل جلاله فلا نعيدها هاهنا.
This section is appropriate to the third chapter, namely that a single act of power falling under the power of two agents is among the possibilities. We only paused at this act due to the necessity of division. If this section is invalidated, the other section is determined: that Allah has power over it just as the servant has power over it, and each one uniquely brings it into existence, as a group among them held. Then, upon this section we compel and say: If the servant brings it into existence, does Allah still have the power to bring it into existence? If they say: Yes, then they have committed an absurdity, because bringing into existence what already exists is impossible. If they say: No, then they have admitted that the servant removed Allah's power from what was established upon it, and prevented Him from bringing into existence what He was able to bring into existence. This is incapacitation according to us, and prevention according to you, and all of that is impossible and inconceivable. And Allah is the Giver of success. The servant. If they say: Allah brings it into existence in the second state from the state of its existence which He brought into existence, it is said: The compulsion in the first state remains, and you have no objection against it. Then bringing it into existence also in the second state is impossible. For what the servant brought into existence with us is impossible to endure, and with you there is disagreement among yourselves: sometimes it may be what endures and sometimes what does not endure. If it is what does not endure, then bringing it into existence in the second state is impossible, because it becomes enduring due to its existence in two successive moments between which non-existence is inconceivable. This is the definition of endurance, and the statement of the endurance of what does not endure is impossible. If it is what endures, then in the second moment of its time of existence it exists, and bringing into existence what exists is impossible. And by these sections it is known that the statement affirming creative power for the servant leads to incapacitating Allah, which is impossible. And we only said that it leads to invalidating the proofs of the monotheists, because it leads to incapacitating the Creator as we have explained. And if it were permissible for the Exalted and Majestic Creator to be incapacitated by others incapacitating Him without His lordship being nullified, then it would be permissible for the world to have two or more makers even if some incapacitated others. And we have thoroughly established this section in the question of proving the oneness of the Pre-Eternal (mighty is His majesty), so we do not repeat it here.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the view that both God and the servant can have creative power over the same act. The author first clarifies the division: the first possibility (two agents for one act) is negated, leaving the second possibility that each agent creates individually without sharing. Then the author poses a dilemma: if the servant creates an act, does God still have power to create that same act? If yes, that would be creating what already exists, which is impossible. If no, then the servant has removed God's power and prevented Him from creating what He was able to create, which is incapacitation (ta'jiz). Both are impossible. The objector suggests God could create it in a second moment. The author responds that the first moment dilemma remains, and creating in the second moment is also impossible because the act is either transitory (so it cannot persist to a second moment) or enduring (so it already exists, and creating it again is impossible). Therefore, affirming creative power for the servant leads to incapacitating God, which is impossible. Furthermore, this leads to invalidating the proofs of tawhid, because if God can be incapacitated, multiple creators become possible. The author refers to his fuller treatment elsewhere.

Key Terms
قدرة التخليق
تعجيز
مقدور واحد
قادرين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that both God and the servant can be full creators of the same act simultaneously.
Correction: This dilemma shows that such a view leads to either creating the existing (impossible) or incapacitating God (impossible), so it is logically untenable.

Checkpoint
According to the dilemma, if the servant creates an act and God no longer has power over that act, what is the consequence?
A) God's power is unaffected.
B) The servant has incapacitated God.
C) The act becomes impossible.
D) Both agents cooperate.

Key Takeaway
Affirming creative power for the servant inevitably leads to the absurd conclusion that either God creates what already exists or the servant incapacitates God; both are impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you make plans, do you ever stop to consider that your ability to act is a gift from Allah, and that He could remove it at any moment? How does this awareness change the way you approach tomorrow?
?
This argument shows that claiming independent creative power for yourself is tantamount to incapacitating Allah. In what areas of your life do you subtly act as if you are the true creator of your successes? What would it look like to genuinely attribute every outcome to Allah?
?
If you truly believed that your power to act is entirely dependent on Allah's permission and that He alone creates the act, how might your reliance on Him increase? What concrete step can you take today to live out this tawheed in your actions?

Refuting the Objection of Sequential Creation
Author refutes an objection and ties to tawhid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the objection that God could create the act in a second moment fails, and how this reinforces the conclusion that affirming creative power for the servant leads to incapacitation of God and undermines tawhid.

Core Idea
Creating the same act in a second moment is impossible whether the act is transitory or enduring.

After the dilemma, the opponent might suggest that God could create the act in a subsequent moment, thus avoiding the charge of creating what already exists. The author anticipates this and offers a detailed refutation. This lesson unpacks that refutation and shows how it further supports the Maturidi position, plus it connects to the broader proof of God's oneness.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
The objector proposes that God creates the act in the second moment of its existence, after the servant has created it in the first moment.
This is a subtle attempt to avoid the dilemma.
2
Analyze the first part of the refutation
Notice the author first reminds that the original dilemma still holds for the first moment. Then he examines the two possibilities for the act's nature: transitory or enduring.
The act cannot be created again if it is transitory (it ceases to exist) or if it is enduring (it already exists).
3
Understand the consequences for tawhid
Read the final paragraph where the author states that this whole argument leads to invalidating the proofs of monotheism, because if God could be incapacitated, multiple creators become possible.
This shows the high stakes of the debate.

Source Text

Checkpoint
According to the refutation, why is it impossible for God to create the act in the second moment if the act is transitory?
A) Because transitory acts do not exist in any moment.
B) Because then it would have to endure across two moments, contradicting its transitory nature.
C) Because God cannot create transitory things.
D) Because the act would be eternal.

Key Takeaway
The objection of sequential creation fails because the act's nature (transitory or enduring) makes second-moment creation impossible, reinforcing that affirming creative power for the servant leads to incapacitating God and ultimately threatens the doctrine of tawhid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever catch yourself feeling that your successes or failures are entirely your own doing, as if you are the creator of your actions? How does this logical argument that such a belief incapacitates Allah force you to reconsider that feeling? Commit today to repeating 'Lā ḥawla wa lā quwwata illā billāh' whenever you sense independence.
?
If it were truly possible for you to create your own acts independently, what would that imply about Allah's lordship over you? How does the impossibility shown here deepen your reliance on Him? Make a habit of acknowledging His power before every action.
?
Think of a moment you were proud of your own effort. Now imagine that attributing that success to your own creative power would be equivalent to incapacitating Allah. Does that thought unsettle you? What practical change will you make to keep that from happening?

The Mu'tazila's Contradictions in Justice and Tawhid
The author exposes the inconsistency in the Mu'tazila position on human creative power and divine justice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Mu'tazila's efforts to protect divine justice and human capacity lead to internal contradictions that undermine both tawhid and justice, as per the Maturidi critique.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila invalidate their justice by their tawhid and their tawhid by their justice.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi exposes the logical inconsistencies in the Mu'tazila position on divine justice and human capacity. He shows that their attempt to avoid implicating God in evil leads them to deny essential divine attributes, which in turn makes command and prohibition meaningless and punishment unjust. The result is a self-defeating theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Note the two main motivations of the Mu'tazila: (1) affirming creative power to avoid God's direct creation of evil, (2) affirming prior capacity to avoid impossible obligation.
The passage ends incompletely; focus on the argument presented.
2
Identify the first contradiction
Notice how affirming creative power (qudrat al-takhlīq) for humans leads to denying that God's speech is a real attribute, thus invalidating tawhid. This is the first contradiction: justice (avoiding divine injustice) undermines tawhid.
3
Analyze the second contradiction
Examine the argument about capacity (istita'a). The Mu'tazila affirm capacity before the act, but then say it ceases at the act. This leads to the agent having no power at the time of action, resulting in impossible obligation (taklif ma la yutaq), which is unjust. Thus, their own doctrine of capacity undermines their justice.
4
Understand the summary statement
The author summarizes that the Mu'tazila invalidate their justice by their tawhid and their tawhid by their justice. Reflect on why this is a key Maturidi critique.
The passage ends with a conditional statement about a world without attributes; though incomplete, the point is clear.

ثم المعتزلة إنما يثبتون لغير الله تعالى قدرة التخليق لئلا يكون الله تعالى معاقبًا عباده على ما يخلق هو بنفسه ويخرجه من العدم إلى الوجود، فيكون عادلاً في تعذيبهم غير ظالم في عقابهم، فأبطلوا التوحيد بهذا العدل، وقد بينا أنهم حيث أنكروا أن يكون الكلام معنى قائمًا بذات الله تعالى أو شيء من الصفات بل قالوا بذات لا صفة له تحقيقا للتوحيد فأبطلوا أمره ونهيه وبطل بذلك الحل والحرمة وخرج الفعل عن كونه طاعة أو معصية، وكان التعذيب على ما ليس بمعصية ظلمًا فأبطلوا عدلهم بتوحيدهم، وهذا معنى قول أصحابنا إن المعتزلة أبطلوا عدلهم بتوحيدهم وتوحيدهم بعدلهم ولو قيل : إنهم أبطلوا عدلهم بعدلهم وتوحيدهم بتوحيدهم لكان صوابًا ، وبيانه أنهم أثبتوا الاستطاعة سابقة على الفعل لئلا يؤدي إلى تكليف ما لا يطاق، ثم قررنا أنها تنعدم عند الفعل فإذا كان فعل عندهم لا قدرة للفاعل عليه، وما لا قدرة للفاعل عليه كان تكليفه تكليف ما لا يطاق، والأمر به والنهي عنه باطل والتعذيب عليه ظلم فأبطلوا عدلهم بعدلهم، وأبطلوا توحيدهم بتوحيدهم، فإنه لو جاز وجود العالم بذات لا حياة له ولا قدرة ولا علم ولا سمع ولا
Then the Mu'tazila only affirm creative power for other than Allah so that Allah is not punishing His servants for what He Himself creates and brings from non-existence into existence, thus He would be just in torturing them, not unjust in punishing them. So they invalidated tawhid (divine unity) by this justice. And we have explained that they, when they denied that speech (kalam) is a meaning subsisting in the essence of Allah or any of the attributes, but rather said a self without attribute as a verification of tawhid, they invalidated His command and prohibition, and thereby permissibility and prohibition became null, and the act came out of being obedience or disobedience, and torture for what is not disobedience would be injustice. So they invalidated their justice by their tawhid. This is the meaning of our companions' statement: 'The Mu'tazila invalidated their justice by their tawhid, and their tawhid by their justice.' And if it were said: 'They invalidated their justice by their justice and their tawhid by their tawhid,' that would be correct. And its explanation is that they affirmed capacity (istita'a) prior to the act so that it does not lead to impossible obligation (taklif ma la yutaq). Then we established that it ceases at the act. So if according to them the act is such that the agent has no power over it, and what the agent has no power over, its imposition is impossible obligation, and commanding and forbidding it are invalid, and torture for it is injustice. So they invalidated their justice by their justice, and they invalidated their tawhid by their tawhid. For if the existence of the world were permissible with an essence having no life, no power, no knowledge, no hearing, and no...
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage critiques the Mu'tazila motivation for affirming human creative power. They assert that humans have creative power (qudrat al-takhlīq) to avoid God punishing people for actions He Himself creates, which would be unjust. But by doing so, they undermine tawhid (divine unity) because they deny that God's attributes (like speech) are real and eternal, reducing God to a bare essence without attributes. This nullifies Allah's commands and prohibitions, making actions neither obedience nor sin, so punishment becomes unjust. Thus, their attempt at justice destroys tawhid, and their attempt at tawhid destroys justice. The author further explains that they also affirm capacity (istitā'a) before the act to avoid impossible obligation, but then hold that capacity vanishes at the time of action, so the agent has no power at the moment of acting, which actually results in impossible obligation. So their justice and tawhid both become self-defeating. The passage ends with a conditional statement that if a world could exist with a being without life, power, knowledge, etc., it would imply absurdities, but the text is cut off.

C) To deny God's attributes.
D) To uphold divine determinism.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila's theological system is internally inconsistent: their concept of justice undermines divine unity, and their concept of tawhid leads to injustice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught yourself adjusting your understanding of Allah's attributes to make His actions fit your sense of fairness? The Mu'tazila sacrificed tawhid to protect their idea of justice. Where might you be doing the same in your own thinking? Ask Allah to grant you submission to His wisdom even when you don't understand.
?
The Mu'tazila's doctrine of capacity was meant to protect humans from being held accountable for what they cannot do. Yet their own reasoning made obligation impossible. Are you, in your spiritual life, overcomplicating obedience with your own conditions and analyses, inadvertently excusing yourself from commands that are actually within your reach? Repent and return to simple submission.
?
When you read that the Mu'tazila invalidated their justice by their tawhid and vice versa, do you see any inconsistency in your own beliefs or practices where one aspect of your faith contradicts another? Perhaps you claim to rely on Allah's decree but act as if your efforts alone decide outcomes. Let this lesson move you to seek consistency and sincerity in your tawhid and your actions.

The Absurdity of Creators Among Creatures
Mu'tazila view that humans create their own acts makes every animal a partner.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Maturidi author argues that the Mu'tazilite view of human self-creation reduces to making every creature a partner with Allah.

Core Idea
If animals create their own acts, they share in divine sovereignty — an absurdity.

The Mu'tazila held that humans create their own actions, a cornerstone of their theology. But what does that imply about other creatures? In this passage, the author reveals the logical consequence: if any living being creates its own act, then dogs, pigs, and insects become partners in creation, limiting Allah's power. This reductio ad absurdum is further sharpened by comparing the Mu'tazila to the Magians and citing a prophetic hadith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the strong language: 'every dog, pig, flea, and mosquito becomes a partner.'
The author uses vivid examples to emphasize the absurdity.
2
Identify the core argument
The passage states: if creatures create their own acts, then those acts are beyond Allah's power, making the creature a partner in sovereignty. Trace this logical move.
The argument is a form of reductio ad absurdum.
3
Analyze the comparison with Magians
The author claims the Mu'tazila imitated the Magians (dualists) and even surpassed them in error. Reflect on why this comparison is made.
The Magians believed in two creators, one good and one evil. The Mu'tazila multiply creators endlessly.
4
Consider the hadith reference
The passage ends with the famous hadith: 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this nation.' Understand the significance of this prophetic condemnation.
This hadith is frequently cited in refutations of the Mu'tazila.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجمهور المعتزلة يجعلون كل فعل حصل من أحد المخلوقين الأحياء باختيارهم مخلوقا لهم خارجا عن مقدور الله تعالى، فيكون كل كلب وخنزير وبق وبعوض شريكًا للمتعالي في العالم بعضه له ما لا قدرة الله عليه وبعضه الله تعالى، فيذهب كل منهم بما خلق، وهؤلاء الجمهور منهم بل كلهم ضاهوا المجوس وأربوا عليهم بوجهين على ما قررنا في إبطال كلام معمر، ولهذا ورد المأثور عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم "القدرية مجوس هذه الأمة".
The majority of the Mu'tazila make every action that occurs from any living creature by their choice created by them, outside the power of Allah. Thus every dog, pig, flea, and mosquito becomes a partner of the Exalted in the world: part of it belongs to that creature, and Allah has no power over it, and part belongs to Allah. Each takes away what it created. These majority, indeed all of them, imitated the Magians and surpassed them in two ways, as we established in refuting the speech of Ma'mar. For this reason the transmitted tradition from the Prophet (peace be upon him) came: 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this nation.'
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage refutes the Mu'tazilite doctrine that humans create their own acts, thereby attributing creative power to animals and other creatures. The author argues that this reduces Allah's power and makes every creature a partner. The Mu'tazila are likened to the Magians, but surpassed them in error. The passage concludes by citing the well-known hadith that the Qadariyya (those who deny divine predestination of acts) are the Magians of the Muslim community.

Key Takeaway
Attributing creative power to any creature necessarily makes that creature a partner with Allah, an impossibility that shows the Mu'tazila error.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Examine your heart: is there a hidden 'I made this happen'? Today, practice saying 'Alhamdulillah' for every small success, acknowledging that even your ability to choose is from Allah.
?
The Mu'tazila were trying to protect human responsibility, but they ended up making dogs and insects partners with Allah. Where in your life do you prioritize your own sense of control over absolute dependence on Allah? Will you surrender that area today by making du'a and then trusting His decree completely?
?
If a mosquito becomes a 'creator' in the Mu'tazila system, then you and I are also setting ourselves up as little gods every time we claim ownership of our deeds. Will you repent from that subtle shirk and commit to attributing every action—good or bad—to Allah's power and will?

Refuting al-Ka'bi: The Maturidi View on Human Action
Refutation of al-Ka'bi's objection and Maturidi position on human action.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Maturidi position on human action as acquisition (iktisab) refutes al-Ka'bi's objection and distinguishes itself from other theological schools.

Core Idea
Human action is God's creation; the servant only acquires it, so there is no resemblance to God's act.

Al-Ka'bi, a Mu'tazili theologian, raised an objection that if humans act like God, their act must resemble God's. But the Maturidi response carefully distinguishes between creation (khalq) and acquisition (iktisab), showing that human acts are entirely God's creation and the servant merely acquires them. This lesson unpacks that refutation and clarifies the Maturidi stance.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read al-Ka'bi's objection carefully. He argues that if we (the Mu'tazila) say our act is like God's but different, while you (Ash'aris/Maturidis) claim to do the very act of God, then you are more deserving of the charge of resemblance.
2
Analyze the response to Ash'aris and Najjariyya
The author points out that the objection does not apply to groups who deny human agency or define act differently. First, Ash'aris who equate act with the object of act deny the servant is an agent, so they cannot be said to do God's act. Second, Najjariyya and Ahl al-Hadith who affirm acquisition but deny creation are not creators like God, so the objection hits the Mu'tazila themselves.
3
Understand the Maturidi position
Read the final part where the author states the Maturidi view: the servant's act is God's created thing (makhluq) and object (maf'ul), not God's eternal attribute. God brings it into existence; the servant acquires and performs it. Thus, there is no similarity.
Note the key distinction between fi'l (act) as God's eternal attribute and maf'ul (object of act) as the created entity.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider how this refutation upholds divine omnipotence while affirming human responsibility through acquisition. Ask yourself: Why is it important to distinguish between creation and acquisition?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا اعتراض الكعبي ذكر في المقالات فإن قالوا إنا إن قلنا: إنا نفعل مثل فعل ربنا، ولكن لا شك أن فعلنا غير فعل ربنا وإنكم تزعمون أنكم تفعلون عين فعل ربكم فأنتم أحق بالقول باشتباه فعلكم بفعل ربكم. قلنا لهم: أما الأشعرية وأبو عيسى البرغوث من النجارية فإنهم إن زعموا أن الفعل عين المفعول فإنهم يأبون أن يكون العبد فاعلاً فلا يستقيم قولكم في حقهم إنكم تفعلون فعل ربكم، فسقط كلامكم في حقهم. ومن قال من النجارية ومتكلمي أهل الحديث: أن العبد يفعل إلا أن فعله الاكتساب لما أحدثه الله تعالى لا الإحداث فهؤلاء وإن قرروا بالفعل ولكن فعلهم ليس بخلق فلم يكونوا خلقوا كخلق الله تعالى وأنتم الخالقون بزعمكم كخلق الله تعالى؛ فلزمكم هذا الكلام وسقط عنهم. وعندنا فعل العبد هو مخلوق الله ومفعوله لا فعله لأن فعل الله تعالى هو الصفة الأزلية القائمة بذاته، وما هو فعل العبد فهو مفعول الله تعالى، والله تعالى هو الذي تولى إيجاده وإخراجه من العدم إلى الوجود، والعبد اكتسبه وباشره فلم يكن فعل العبد مثل فعله ولا خلقه كخلقه، وكيف يكون كذلك ولا خلق للعبد البتة.
This is the objection of al-Ka'bi mentioned in al-Maqalat. If they say: 'We indeed say that we do like the act of our Lord, but there is no doubt that our act is other than the act of our Lord, and you claim that you do the very act of your Lord, so you are more deserving of saying that your act resembles His act.' We say to them: As for the Ash'aris and Abu 'Isa al-Barghuth from the Najjariyya, if they claim that the act is identical to the object of the act, then they refuse that the servant is an agent, so your statement that you do the act of your Lord does not hold regarding them, so your speech falls regarding them. As for those from the Najjariyya and the mutakallimun of Ahl al-Hadith who say that the servant does act, but his act is acquisition (iktisab) of what God has originated, not origination (ihdath) itself: these, even if they are affirmed as acting, their act is not creation (khalq), so they are not creators like the creation of God. But you are creators, in your claim, like the creation of God, so this speech applies to you and falls away from them. According to us, the act of the servant is the created thing (makhluq) of God and His object of act (maf'ul), not His act, because the act of God is the eternal attribute subsisting in His essence. What is the act of the servant is the object of act of God. God alone undertook its bringing into existence and bringing it out from non-existence to existence. The servant acquired (iktasaba) it and performed it directly (bashara). So the act of the servant is not like His act, nor is his creation like His creation. How could it be so, when there is no creation for the servant at all?
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage refutes an objection by al-Ka'bi and presents the Maturidi position on human action. The objector argues: if we (the Mu'tazila) say we do an act like God's act, but admit our act is different from God's, whereas you (the Ash'aris and Maturidis) claim to do the very act of God (i.e., you attribute creation to God alone and deny human agency), then you are more deserving of claiming resemblance. The author responds by distinguishing two groups: (1) The Ash'aris and Abu 'Isa al-Barghuth (a Najjari) who say act is identical to the object of act (so God's act is the created thing) and deny that the servant is a true agent—against them, the objection does not apply because they do not claim the servant does God's act. (2) The Najjariyya and Ahl al-Hadith mutakallimun who say the servant acts but his act is acquisition (iktisab) of what God originates, not origination itself—these groups do not claim to create like God, so the objection falls on the Mu'tazila themselves who claim to be creators like God. Then the author states the Maturidi position: the servant's act is the created thing (makhluq) of God, not God's act (fi'l), because God's act is His eternal attribute subsisting in His essence. God alone brings it into existence; the servant acquires (iktisab) it and directly performs it (mubashara). Thus, there is no similarity between divine and human acts, and the servant has no creative power at all.

Key Terms

صفة أزلية

فاعل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Maturidi position on human action is identical to the Ash'ari position (both deny human agency).
Correction: The Maturidis affirm that the servant acts through acquisition (iktisab) and direct performance (mubashara), though the act itself is God's creation. This differs from the Ash'ari view that the act is identical to its object and the servant is not an agent.

Checkpoint

B) Because Maturidis hold that the servant's act is God's creation and the servant only acquires it, so the servant does not create like God.
C) Because Maturidis deny that God creates human acts.
D) Because Maturidis are not mentioned in the passage.

Key Takeaway
The servant's act is entirely God's creation; the servant only acquires it, so there is no resemblance to God's act and no human creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you truly internalize that God created that action and you only acquired it? How would that change your shame and your hope for forgiveness?
?
If you have no creative power over your deeds, what is left for you to boast about? How does this lesson strip away your pride in your good deeds?
?
Do you live as if you originate your actions or as if you merely acquire them? What practice can you adopt this week to remind yourself that God alone creates, and you are only the acquirer?

Refuting the Objection of Compulsion and Divine Weakness
Nasafi refutes the objection of compulsion and divine weakness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Nasafi refutes the objection that the Maturidi position on human action leads to compulsion or divine inability.

Core Idea
The Maturidi view preserves both divine power and human choice.

Nasafi now takes up a common objection against the Maturidi position on human action. Critics argue that if God creates all actions, humans are either compelled or God is limited. In this passage, Nasafi shows why the objection fails, grounding his response in the established proofs of God's creative power and human acquisition.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the first paragraph of the passage, which presents the opponents' argument. Note the two horns of the dilemma: either the servant has power to refuse (making God incapable) or the servant is compelled.
The objection is based on the assumption that if God creates the act, the servant cannot have real power.
2
Identify Nasafi's initial reply
Nasafi responds by stating that they have already established by proof that God is the creator and the servant is an acquirer. The objection would require invalidating one of these certain proofs, which is impossible.
Nasafi does not re-prove the position; he asserts its certainty.
3
Understand the distinction between movements
Nasafi distinguishes necessary movement (where the servant has no power of refusal) from voluntary movement (where the servant wills and chooses). For voluntary actions, refusal is impossible because the act exists concurrent with the servant's power.
This distinction shows that compulsion applies only to necessary actions, not to voluntary ones.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى هذا الوجه يبطل أيضًا قولهم إن ما قلتم يؤدي إلى جعل العباد مضطرين أو إلى تعجيز الله تعالى فإن الله تعالى إذا أراد أن يخلق كسب العبد إن كان للعبد قوة الامتناع فقد عجز الله تعالى عن تخليقه وإن لم يكن له قدرة الامتناع فهو إذًا مضطر

فإنا نقول: ثبتنا بالدليل أن لا اختراع من قبل العبد وأن له فعلاً كان مجموع الدليلين موجبًا كونه تعالى قادرًا مخترعًا، وكون العبد فاعلاً مكتسبًا مختارا.

وما قلتم من السؤال يوجب بطلان أحد هذين الوجهين، وما ثبت بالدليل المتيقن غير محتمل للبطلان، فإذا كان السؤال في نفسه باطلاً.

ثم نقول: إن كان الله تعالى أراد الحركة الضرورية من العبد فيخلقه ولا يكون للعبد قدرة الامتناع والله تعالى قادر والعبد مضطر، وإن أراد تخليق الحركة الاختيارية فالعبد لا يتصور منه الامتناع لأنه تعالى إنما يخلق تلك الحركة إذا أرادها العبد واختار وقصد اكتسابها فيخلق الله تعالى لا محالة لإجرائه العادة في تخليقه عند وجود قصد العبد لا لكونه ملجأ إلى ذلك، على أن الله تعالى إذا كان يخلقه مقارنا لقدرة العبد كيف يتصور منه الامتناع عن الفعل وهو موجود والامتناع عن الموجود محال، والله الموفق.
And in this way their statement is also invalidated: What you say leads to making servants compelled or to making God incapable. For if God intends to create the acquisition (kasb) of the servant, if the servant has the power of refusal, then God is incapable of creating it, and if he does not have the power of refusal, then he is compelled.

So we say: We have established by proof that there is no creation from the servant, and that he has an act that is a combination of two proofs: that He (God) is powerful and creator, and that the servant is an acting, acquiring, choosing agent.

And what you said in the objection necessitates the invalidation of one of these two aspects. And what is established by certain proof is not subject to invalidation. So the objection is itself invalid.

Then we say: If God intends the necessary movement from the servant, He creates it, and the servant does not have the power of refusal, and God is powerful and the servant is compelled. And if He intends to create the voluntary movement, then the servant cannot be imagined to refuse, because He only creates that movement when the servant wills it and chooses and intends to acquire it. So God creates it necessarily due to His customary practice of creating it upon the existence of the servant's intention, not because He is compelled to do so. Moreover, since God creates it concurrent with the servant's power, how can refusal be imagined from him while the act exists? And refusal of something existent is impossible. And God is the granter of success.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage refutes an objection from opponents (likely Mu'tazila) who argue that the Maturidi view (that human actions are created by God and acquired by humans) leads to either compulsion of humans or making God incapable. The author first presents the objection: if God wants to create the servant's kasb (acquisition), if the servant has the power to refuse (quwwat al-imtina'), then God is incapable of creating it; if not, then the servant is compelled. The author responds by asserting that they have already proven by proof (dalil) that there is no creation (ikhtira') from the servant, yet the servant has an act that is a combination of two proofs (majmu' al-dalilayn): God is the powerful creator, and the servant is an acting, acquiring, choosing agent. The objection would require invalidating one of these two established aspects, but they are proven by certain proof (al-dalil al-mutayaqqan), so the objection is invalid. He then elaborates: If God intends necessary motion (al-haraka al-daruriyya), the servant has no power of refusal, so the servant is compelled (but that is not the case for voluntary actions). For voluntary actions (al-haraka al-ikhtiyariyya), God creates the movement only when the servant wills it and intends to acquire it, so refusal is impossible because the act exists concurrent with the servant's power, and refusal of an existent is impossible. Thus, the objection is based on a misunderstanding of the Maturidi position.

Key Terms
مضطر
تعجيز
كسب
اختراع
قوة الامتناع
حركة ضرورية
حركة اختيارية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Maturidism negates human freedom and makes humans compelled.
Correction: Nasafi distinguishes necessary movements (where compulsion is acknowledged) from voluntary movements, where the servant genuinely wills and chooses, and God creates the act concurrent with that choice.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, why does the objection about compulsion fail?
A) Because the servant has independent creative power
B) Because the established proof of servant's acquisition and God's creation is certain and cannot be invalidated
C) Because God is not capable of creating human actions
D) Because the objection is not logical

Key Takeaway
Nasafi shows that the objection is based on a misunderstanding: voluntary actions involve genuine choice and acquisition, not compulsion, and the certainty of the established proofs makes the objection invalid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you ever catch yourself thinking, 'God made me do it' or 'It was out of my control'? How does this lesson’s distinction between necessary and voluntary movements challenge that excuse? Will you now own your choices fully, even when they are wrong?
?
If you truly believe that every good deed you do is a creation of Allah that He brings into existence concurrent with your intention, does that fill you with humility or pride? How can you cultivate gratitude for the ability to acquire good deeds, knowing that the act itself is from Allah?
?
This lesson says that for voluntary actions, refusal is impossible because the act exists with your power. Does your daily experience of hesitation or regret before sinning contradict this? Are you willing to admit that your 'feeling of being forced' is often a cover for your own choice? What will you do the next time you feel tempted to blame your circumstances for a sin?

One Act Under Two Powers: Responding to the Mu'tazila
Al-Nasafi proves one act under two powers and questions the Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi argument that a single act can be under both God's creative power and the servant's acquired power, and how this refutes the Mu'tazila position.

Core Idea
A single act can be created by God and acquired by the servant.

The Mu'tazila argued that one act cannot be under two powers. Imam al-Nasafi responds by clarifying that the act is under God's creative power and the servant's acquired power — two different aspects. This lesson walks through his proof and the key refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get its flow, then read the literal translation. Note how the author builds his argument.
The passage is dense but follows a clear logical order.
2
Identify the two aspects of power
Look for the distinction between 'invention' (ikhtira') and 'acquisition' (iktisab). This distinction is key to the argument.
The author agrees impossibility if both powers are of the same kind.
3
Understand the refutation of Mu'tazila
See how the author questions the Mu'tazila: they have no proof except imagination (wahm). They must specify which aspect they mean.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبالوقوف على ما بينا من دليل استحالة ثبوت قدرة التخليق للعبد، ودليل ثبوت الفعل والقدرة له يعرف جواز دخول مقدور واحد تحت قدرة قادرين بحمد الله تعالى دليل فيه كفاية وغنية عن الاشتغال بغيره من الدلائل. ثم نقول: قد سبق منا القول في الفصل الذي أثبتنا فيه استحالة دخول الاختراع تحت قدرة العبد، وأن إقدار الغير على ما لا يقدر عليه المقدر محال، وقد انعقد الإجماع أن الله تعالى هو الذي يقدر العبد ويخلق قدرته، وأن القدرة ليست بداخله تحت قدرة العبد إذ لو منعت منه لما تمكن من اكتسابها عندنا وتخليقها عندهم، وإذا كان الله تعالى هو الذي يقدر العبد كان محالاً أن يقدره على ما لا قدرة له عليه على ما قررنا، فكان ذلك دليلاً على جواز دخول مقدور واحد تحت قدرة قادرين، ثم لا دليل يدل للمعتزلة على استحالة دخول مقدور واحد تحت قدرة قادرين، إلا أنهم لم يعاينوا ذلك وهم أبدا يفزعون إلى الوهم ويجعلونه عيارا للعقل والفهم وهو بعيد عن الصواب على ما قررنا. ثم قيل لهم أيش تعنون بقولكم إن دخول مقدور واحد تحت قدرة قاردين محال ؟ أتعنون دخوله من جهة الاختراع أو من جهة الاكتساب أو من جهة اكتساب و اختراع؟ فإن قالوا من جهة الاختراع فسلم تنازعهم في هذا، وإن قالوا: من جهة الاكتساب فكذلك لأن فعلاً واحدًا لا يكون فعلا لكاسبين. وإن قالوا من جهة الاكتساب والاختراع أن يقدر على اختراعه مخترع وعلى اكتسابه مكتسب ففيه النزاع.
And by considering what we have explained of the proof of the impossibility of establishing the power of invention (takhliq) for the servant, and the proof of the establishment of action and power for him, one knows the permissibility of one act of power (maqdur) falling under two powers (qadirayn), by the praise of God, a proof sufficient and independent of engaging with other proofs. Then we say: We have already stated in the chapter in which we established the impossibility of invention (ikhtira') falling under the servant's power, and that empowering another over what the empowerer cannot do is impossible. And consensus has been reached that God, exalted, is the one who empowers the servant and creates his power, and that power (qudra) is itself not within the servant's power—for if it were prevented from him, he would not be able to acquire it according to us, nor create it according to them. And if God is the one who empowers the servant, it is impossible that He empower him over what he has no power over, as we have established. So that was a proof for the permissibility of one act of power falling under two powers. Then there is no proof for the Mu'tazila indicating the impossibility of one act of power falling under two powers, except that they have not witnessed that, and they always flee to imagination (wahm) and make it the criterion for intellect and understanding, and that is far from correctness as we have established. Then it was said to them: What do you mean by your statement that the entry of one act of power under two powers is impossible? Do you mean its entry from the aspect of invention (ikhtira'), or from the aspect of acquisition (iktisab), or from the aspect of acquisition and invention? If they say from the aspect of invention, then we concede their dispute in this. And if they say from the aspect of acquisition, likewise because a single act cannot be an act for two acquirers. And if they say from the aspect of acquisition and invention, i.e., that an inventor has power over its invention and an acquirer over its acquisition, then therein lies the dispute.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage is a proof and a refutation of the Mu'tazila position that one act cannot be under two powers. The author begins by stating that considering the earlier proofs—that the servant cannot have creative power (takhliq) but does have action and power—leads to the conclusion that one act of power (maqdur) can be under two powers. This proof is sufficient and needs no other. Then he reiterates that invention (ikhtira') is impossible under the servant's power, and empowering someone over what the empowerer cannot do is impossible. Consensus holds that God empowers the servant and creates his power; the servant's power itself is not under his control. Since God empowers the servant, He cannot empower him over what he has no power over (i.e., creation). Thus one act can be under God's creative power and the servant's acquired power. The Mu'tazila have no proof against this; they rely on imagination (wahm) as a criterion, which is erroneous. Then the author poses a question: What exactly do you mean by impossibility? If you mean from the aspect of invention, we agree; if from acquisition, also agreed (one act cannot be acquired by two). But if you mean from both aspects—invented by one and acquired by another—that is the point of dispute, and our proofs support it.

Key Terms
مقدور
قدرة
قادران
اختراع
اكتساب
وهم
إجماع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: It is always impossible for one act to be under two powers.
Correction: It is only impossible if both powers are of the same kind (both creative or both acquisitive). It is possible if one is creative and the other acquisitive.

Checkpoint
What does the author identify as the Mu'tazila's faulty criterion for rejecting one act under two powers?
A) Consensus
B) Imagination (wahm)
C) Reason
D) Scripture

Key Takeaway
One act can be under two powers as long as the powers are of different types: creative (God) and acquisitive (servant).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you accomplish something good, do you secretly believe it was entirely your own doing, or do you truly feel that God enabled you? How might this lesson's distinction between creation and acquisition change your next prayer of gratitude?
?
The Mu'tazila relied on what seemed plausible to their imagination rather than on divine revelation and sound reasoning. In what area of your faith are you tempted to trust your own assumptions over what God has clearly taught? Will you actively submit that area to the truth of this lesson today?
?
If God creates both the act and your power to acquire it, then your will is not independent—yet you are still responsible. Does this truth humble you or trouble you? How will you live differently now that you know your every good deed is a gift both created by God and acquired by you?

The Trilemma on Created Acts
Nasafi presents a trilemma for the opponent on generated acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical trilemma that the Maturidi author uses to force the opponent to either accept the Sunni position on created acts or face logical inconsistency.

Core Idea
The opponent must choose: accept Sunni doctrine, accept dual agency, or be stubborn—none consistent with their own premises.

Imam Nasafi presents a decisive logical trilemma to the opponent who denies that God creates all human acts. The trilemma shows that the opponent's own principles lead to an unavoidable choice: either recant, contradict themselves, or persist in pure obstinacy. This argument powerfully defends the Sunni position on divine omnipotence.

Guided Path
1
Read the trilemma passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice that the author addresses the opponent directly using 'you'.
The passage is a single sentence but packs a complete argument.
2
Identify the three options
Find the three options the author presents: (1) recant and adopt the Sunni view, (2) accept dual agency (two powers on one act), (3) cling to both doctrines stubbornly.
Each option is introduced with 'إما أن'.
3
Understand the logical force
For each option, consider why it is problematic for the opponent. The first requires abandoning their doctrine, the second contradicts their own principle that only one agent acts, the third is irrational obstinacy.
4
Reflect on the defense of Sunni doctrine
Realize that the trilemma demonstrates that the Sunni position (all acts from God) is the only logically consistent stance within the opponent's own framework.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم بعد ذلك إنك بين أمور ثلاثة: إما أن ترجع عن مسألة المتولدات وتجعلها الله تعالى كما هو مذهب أهل السنة، أو تجيز تعلق قدرتين بمقدور واحد وجعل شيء فعلاً لفاعلين وفيه رجوع عن مذهبك، أو تتمسك بالمذهبين مع لزوم الدليل فتوصف بالعناد المحض، والله الموفق.
Then after that you are among three matters: either you recant on the issue of generated acts and attribute them to God Almighty as is the doctrine of Ahl al-Sunna, or you permit the attachment of two powers to a single possible object and make something an act of two agents – and in that is a retraction from your doctrine, or you adhere to both doctrines while the proof necessitates [contradiction] and you are described as pure obstinacy. And God is the giver of success.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage is a logical trilemma presented to the opponent (likely a Mu'tazilite) who holds that acts are generated by creatures and that God's power does not directly produce human acts. The author gives three options: (1) Abandon the doctrine of generated acts (mutawallidat) and attribute all acts to God, as Ahl al-Sunna do. (2) Accept that two powers can attach to one act (i.e., both God and the creature act) – but this contradicts the opponent's own principle. (3) Cling stubbornly to both positions despite the logical consequence, which is pure obstinacy. The tone is conclusive, forcing the opponent to concede.

Key Terms
متولدات
قدرتين
مقدور واحد
فاعلين
عناد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The trilemma is a rhetorical trick with no real logical force.
Correction: The trilemma is a valid logical deduction from the opponent's own premises; each option follows necessarily from the opponent's commitments.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the three options the author presents to the opponent?
A) Return to the Sunni position on created acts.
B) Deny the existence of God altogether.
C) Accept that two powers can act on one object.
D) Insist stubbornly on both doctrines.

Key Takeaway
The trilemma shows that the Mu'tazilite position on created acts is logically untenable; the only consistent position is the Sunni doctrine that God creates all acts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

This lesson forces a choice: will you submit to the truth even if it means abandoning a comfortable or familiar position? Examine your heart—are you willing to surrender your intellect and desires to the decisive proof of revelation, or do you cling to what you are used to?
?
The trilemma presents three options, each requiring humility: admitting error, accepting a difficult doctrine, or being labeled obstinate. Which of these do you find hardest in your own life when confronted with truth? 

How does your pride or desire for consistency prevent you from saying, 'I was wrong; I now accept God's word completely'? Ask Allah for the strength to be among those who recant falsehood without hesitation.
?
This passage ends with 'والله الموفق'—success is from God alone. Have you ever sought guidance sincerely when faced with a difficult theological or moral choice, or did you rely on your own reasoning? 

Commit today to make duas for divine guidance in matters where your intellect alone cannot reach certainty, especially in issues of 'aqeedah.
