The Mu'tazila Dilemma: Good Actions and Divine Creation
Nasafi presents a dilemma forcing Mu'tazila to admit divine creation of good actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Nasafi forces the Mu'tazila into a logical dilemma regarding the divine creation of good actions.

Core Idea
If God cannot create evil, consistency demands He creates good actions.

Imam Nasafi begins by noting that a true seeker will not be intimidated by Mu'tazila threats. He then adopts a lenient approach to expose their inconsistency: the Mu'tazila deny that Allah creates evil actions because evil cannot be attributed to Him, but they affirm that good actions (acts of obedience) are by Allah's will. Nasafi presents a dilemma that forces them to either accept that Allah creates good actions, contradict their own doctrine, or deny the Quranic text.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening statement
Read the first sentence carefully. It sets the tone: the truth is clear to those who understand, and they will not be swayed by threats.
Notice the confidence in the author's tone.
2
Grasp the Mu'tazila obstacle
Identify the main obstacle the Mu'tazila claim: they cannot attribute evil to Allah. This is their reason for denying that Allah creates actions.
3
Understand the dilemma
Nasafi asks: if evil is the obstacle, then why do you not affirm that Allah creates good actions, since there is no obstacle there? This forces them to either accept creation of good actions or reject that good actions are by Allah's will.
This is the core of the argument.
4
Analyze the three options
Find the three options Nasafi gives to the Mu'tazila. Each option leads to a problem for their position.
The verse 'Doer of what He wills' is used as evidence.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Consider why Nasafi ends this section with 'Fīhi mā fīhi' (There is that in it). What is he implying about the absurdity of their position?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقف على ما بينا من الوجوه عرف الحقيقة ولم يجبن عن إثبات ذلك عند تهويل المعتزلة، ويبين لهم أنه يقول ما يقولون هم، ويضطر جميع العقلاء إلى القول به.

ثم هذا كله منا جرى مع الخصوم على طريق المساهلة فلو مانعناهم وقلنا: هذا منكم تعيين لبعض فصول الخلاف فإن كان المانع لكم من القول بخلق الأفعال بقدر استحالة إضافة القبيح إلى الله تعالى فما المانع لكم في إضافة الطاعات إلى الله تعالى وهي حكم ومحاسن ؟ فقولوا بخلقها لانعدام هذا المانع فيها وإلا ظهر تعنتكم، على أن عندكم كانت الطاعات كلها بإرادة الله تعالى والله تعالى يقول : فَعّال لِمَا يُرِيدُ فكانت الطاعات مفعولة له لأنها مرادة له وهو يقول: فَقَالَ لِمَا يُرِيدُ فإما أن يقروا بكون الطاعات مخلوقة له، وإما أن يقولوا إنها ليست بإرادته فيبطلون مذهبهم، وإما أن يقولوا إنها وإن كانت إرادة له فلم يفعلها وينكرون النص ويردونه، وفيه ما فيه.

ثم نقول : لا شك أن حسن الطاعات فوق حسن الأجسام، لأن حسنها حسن وهو يختلف باختلاف الحواس على أن عند المعتزلة لا وجه للقول بحسن الأجسام لإنكارهم قبح ما قبح منها وإن عرف ذلك بالحس، فكذا يلزمهم إنكار الحس إذ لا يعرف إلا بما يعرف به القبح، ولا حقيقة لتلك المعرفة فكذا لهذه، وحسن الطاعات عقلي وهو مما لا يختلف باختلاف العقول ولا يستبدل بحال وحال، وتفاضل الفاعلين بتفاضل الأفعال فينبغي أن يكون كل عبد مطيع أفضل من الله تعالى وأحسن فعلاً وأرفع درجة لعلو رتبة فعله على فعل الله تعالى، وانحطاط رتبة فعله عز وجل عن أفعال العباد، ويكون في مقدور العبد من المحاسن ما ليس يماثل ذلك أو يقاربه في مقدور الله تعالى، والقول به قول لا خفاء بما فيه، فكان مقدور الله تعالى هو إبليس والقردة والأقذار والأنتان والزمانة والعمى والشلل والأمراض و الموت والمصائب ومقدور العبد الصوم والصلاة والحج والإقراض والتصديق واعتقاد التوحيد والإفضال إلى المحتاجين والإحسان إليهم والوفاء بالعهود وأداء الأمانات والجود والسماحة، وغير ذلك من الفضائل الداخلة تحت قدرة العباد، تقدر كل واحد من الفاعلين بمقدور ، وذهب بما خلق وفاز العبد بالقسم الأحسن والحظ الأجزل، وقصرت قدرة القديم عن ذلك، ولعلم المعتزلة بهذا الإلزام يعرضون عن جانب المحاسن صفحًا ويتشبثون بالمقابح ليتمكنوا عسى من ترويج باطلهم على ضعفاء المسلمين عصمنا الله تعالى عن ذلك بكرمه وفضله وهو ذو الفضل العظيم.
He who pauses at the aspects we have explained knows the truth and does not shy away from affirming it when the Mu'tazila threaten, and he shows them that he says what they say, and he compels all rational people to affirm it.

Then all this from us proceeded with the opponents on the path of leniency. For if we argue with them and say: This from you is specifying some points of dispute. If the obstacle preventing you from saying that actions are created by decree is the impossibility of attributing evil to Allah, then what prevents you from attributing acts of obedience to Allah, while they are judgments and goods? So say that He creates them due to the absence of this obstacle in them, otherwise your obstinacy becomes apparent. Moreover, according to you, all acts of obedience are by the will of Allah, and Allah says: 'Doer of what He wills' (Hud 11:107). So the acts of obedience are His effects because they are willed by Him. So either they affirm that acts of obedience are created by Him, or they say they are not by His will and thus nullify their own doctrine, or they say that although they are His will, He did not do them, and they deny the text and reject it, and there is that in it.

Then we say: There is no doubt that the goodness of acts of obedience surpasses the goodness of bodies, because their goodness is goodness, and it varies according to the senses, although according to the Mu'tazila there is no way to say that bodies are good because they deny the evil of what is evil among them, even if that is known by sense. So likewise they must deny sense, for it is not known except by what evil is known, and there is no reality for that knowledge, so likewise for this. And the goodness of acts of obedience is rational, and it is something that does not vary according to intellects nor change from state to state. And the superiority of agents is by the superiority of actions, so it would be necessary that every obedient servant be better than Allah, more excellent in action, and higher in rank due to the elevation of his action over Allah's action, and the lowering of the rank of His action over the actions of servants. And in the power of the servant there would be goods that do not resemble or approach that which is in the power of Allah. To say this is a saying the content of which is not hidden. So what is in the power of Allah is Iblis, monkeys, filth, stench, chronic illness, blindness, paralysis, diseases, death, and calamities, and what is in the power of the servant is fasting, prayer, pilgrimage, lending, verification, belief in tawhid, kindness to the needy, charity to them, fulfillment of covenants, discharge of trusts, generosity, and magnanimity, and other virtues that fall under the power of servants. Each one of the agents is empowered according to what is in his power, and he (the servant) takes what he created and wins the best portion and the greatest lot, while the power of the Pre-eternal falls short of that. And because the Mu'tazila know this (as a refutation), they turn away from the side of goods completely and cling to evils so that they might possibly propagate their falsehood upon the weak Muslims. May Allah protect us from that by His generosity and bounty; He is the Possessor of mighty bounty.
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila regarding the divine creation of human actions. The author proceeds as follows:

First, he states that one who understands the proofs previously presented will recognize the truth and not be intimidated by Mu'tazila threats. He will show them that he agrees with some of their premises but reaches different conclusions.

Then, adopting a lenient approach (musāhala), he poses a dilemma: The Mu'tazila deny that Allah creates evil actions because evil cannot be attributed to Allah. But they affirm that good actions (acts of obedience) are by Allah's will. Therefore, consistency demands they affirm that Allah creates these good actions, since there is no obstacle of evil. If they refuse, they are obstinate.

The author strengthens this by citing the Quranic verse 'Doer of what He wills' (Hud 11:107). Since acts of obedience are willed by Allah, they are His effects. The Mu'tazila have three options: (1) admit that Allah creates them, (2) deny they are by His will (which contradicts their own position), or (3) deny the textual evidence.

Next, the author argues that the goodness of acts of obedience is superior to the goodness of physical objects. Goodness of objects is sensory and varies, but the Mu'tazila cannot even affirm sensory goodness because they deny sensory evil. The goodness of obedience is rational and unchanging.

Then comes a reductio ad absurdum: If agents are superior based on the superiority of their actions, then every obedient servant would be better than Allah, since his good deeds are better than what the Mu'tazila claim Allah creates (only evil, filth, etc.). This leads to blasphemous implications: Allah's power would be limited to creating evil and defective things, while the servant's power includes all virtuous deeds. The conclusion is that the Mu'tazila, aware of this devastating objection, avoid discussing good deeds and cling to the discussion of evil to deceive the weak.

The passage ends with a supplication for protection from such deviation.

Key Terms
خلق الأفعال
المعتزلة
الطاعات
القبيح
الإرادة
فعال لما يريد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila think their denial of divine creation of actions is consistent, but they fail to apply the same reasoning to good actions.
Correction: Nasafi shows that the same reasoning that prevents them from attributing evil to Allah should lead them to attribute good actions to Allah, since both are based on moral attributes.

Checkpoint
What is the main point of the dilemma Nasafi presents to the Mu'tazila?
A) They must explain why good actions are not created by Allah given their own premise.
B) They must prove that evil actions are not created.
C) They must show that the Quranic verse is abrogated.
D) They must admit that Allah creates both good and evil.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi exposes the Mu'tazila inconsistency by using their own premise: if evil prevents divine creation, then good actions should be attributed to Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever catch yourself attributing your good deeds to your own strength while blaming your failures on circumstances or others? How does this lesson's focus on Allah creating every act of obedience challenge you to see your entire life—both successes and struggles—as entirely from Him? What would it take for you to sincerely say 'Allah created this good action in me' before every prayer, every kind word, every moment of patience?
?
The Mu'tazila were inconsistent: they denied that Allah creates evil but also refused to admit He creates good. Where in your heart do you show a similar inconsistency—affirming Allah's control in some areas of your life (like your provision or your health) but resisting it in others (like your private sins or your relationships)? What would it look like to surrender that last area today?
?
If you truly believed that every single act of obedience you perform is directly created by Allah—not just permitted or enabled, but created—how would that change your humility before Him? Would you still feel proud of your worship? Would you still despair over your shortcomings? Write down one specific way you will actively remind yourself of this truth in your next act of worship.

The Absurd Conclusion: Would a Servant Be Better Than God?
Nasafi uses reductio ad absurdum to show Mu'tazila view implies servant's superiority over God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the reductio ad absurdum argument that if actions determine superiority, the Mu'tazila position would imply servants are better than God.

Core Idea
If actions define superiority, the servant's good deeds would surpass God's, which is blasphemous.

Having established the dilemma about good actions, Nasafi now takes the argument further. He argues that the goodness of acts of obedience is far superior to the goodness of physical objects. Since moral goodness is rational and objective, and since the superiority of agents is based on their actions, the Mu'tazila view would lead to the absurd conclusion that every obedient servant is better than Allah. He then lists the kinds of things the Mu'tazila claim are in God's power (only evil and defective things) versus what is in the servant's power (all virtues), reinforcing the absurdity.

Guided Path
1
Compare goodness of actions and bodies
Read how Nasafi compares the goodness of acts of obedience with the goodness of physical objects. Notice his reasoning that the goodness of obedience is rational and unchanging.
He also criticizes the Mu'tazila for denying sensory knowledge of good and evil.
2
Understand the principle of superiority
Identify the principle: 'The superiority of agents is by the superiority of their actions.' This leads to the reductio.
3
Trace the reductio ad absurdum
Follow the logic: if superiority is by actions, then the servant's good actions would make him better than Allah, since the servant's actions are good while Allah's actions (according to Mu'tazila) are only evil or neutral.
This is a powerful refutation.
4
Examine the lists of what is in God's power vs. servant's power
Nasafi contrasts the contents of divine and human power. Notice the stark difference: God's power supposedly contains only evil, filth, and defects, while the servant's power contains all virtues.
This highlights the absurdity of the Mu'tazila position.
5
Reflect on the Mu'tazila response
Nasafi notes that the Mu'tazila, aware of this devastating critique, avoid discussing good deeds and cling to the discussion of evil to deceive the weak.
The lesson ends with a supplication for protection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقف على ما بينا من الوجوه عرف الحقيقة ولم يجبن عن إثبات ذلك عند تهويل المعتزلة، ويبين لهم أنه يقول ما يقولون هم، ويضطر جميع العقلاء إلى القول به.

ثم هذا كله منا جرى مع الخصوم على طريق المساهلة فلو مانعناهم وقلنا: هذا منكم تعيين لبعض فصول الخلاف فإن كان المانع لكم من القول بخلق الأفعال بقدر استحالة إضافة القبيح إلى الله تعالى فما المانع لكم في إضافة الطاعات إلى الله تعالى وهي حكم ومحاسن ؟ فقولوا بخلقها لانعدام هذا المانع فيها وإلا ظهر تعنتكم، على أن عندكم كانت الطاعات كلها بإرادة الله تعالى والله تعالى يقول : فَعّال لِمَا يُرِيدُ فكانت الطاعات مفعولة له لأنها مرادة له وهو يقول: فَقَالَ لِمَا يُرِيدُ فإما أن يقروا بكون الطاعات مخلوقة له، وإما أن يقولوا إنها ليست بإرادته فيبطلون مذهبهم، وإما أن يقولوا إنها وإن كانت إرادة له فلم يفعلها وينكرون النص ويردونه، وفيه ما فيه.

ثم نقول : لا شك أن حسن الطاعات فوق حسن الأجسام، لأن حسنها حسن وهو يختلف باختلاف الحواس على أن عند المعتزلة لا وجه للقول بحسن الأجسام لإنكارهم قبح ما قبح منها وإن عرف ذلك بالحس، فكذا يلزمهم إنكار الحس إذ لا يعرف إلا بما يعرف به القبح، ولا حقيقة لتلك المعرفة فكذا لهذه، وحسن الطاعات عقلي وهو مما لا يختلف باختلاف العقول ولا يستبدل بحال وحال، وتفاضل الفاعلين بتفاضل الأفعال فينبغي أن يكون كل عبد مطيع أفضل من الله تعالى وأحسن فعلاً وأرفع درجة لعلو رتبة فعله على فعل الله تعالى، وانحطاط رتبة فعله عز وجل عن أفعال العباد، ويكون في مقدور العبد من المحاسن ما ليس يماثل ذلك أو يقاربه في مقدور الله تعالى، والقول به قول لا خفاء بما فيه، فكان مقدور الله تعالى هو إبليس والقردة والأقذار والأنتان والزمانة والعمى والشلل والأمراض و الموت والمصائب ومقدور العبد الصوم والصلاة والحج والإقراض والتصديق واعتقاد التوحيد والإفضال إلى المحتاجين والإحسان إليهم والوفاء بالعهود وأداء الأمانات والجود والسماحة، وغير ذلك من الفضائل الداخلة تحت قدرة العباد، تقدر كل واحد من الفاعلين بمقدور ، وذهب بما خلق وفاز العبد بالقسم الأحسن والحظ الأجزل، وقصرت قدرة القديم عن ذلك، ولعلم المعتزلة بهذا الإلزام يعرضون عن جانب المحاسن صفحًا ويتشبثون بالمقابح ليتمكنوا عسى من ترويج باطلهم على ضعفاء المسلمين عصمنا الله تعالى عن ذلك بكرمه وفضله وهو ذو الفضل العظيم.
He who pauses at the aspects we have explained knows the truth and does not shy away from affirming it when the Mu'tazila threaten, and he shows them that he says what they say, and he compels all rational people to affirm it.

Then all this from us proceeded with the opponents on the path of leniency. For if we argue with them and say: This from you is specifying some points of dispute. If the obstacle preventing you from saying that actions are created by decree is the impossibility of attributing evil to Allah, then what prevents you from attributing acts of obedience to Allah, while they are judgments and goods? So say that He creates them due to the absence of this obstacle in them, otherwise your obstinacy becomes apparent. Moreover, according to you, all acts of obedience are by the will of Allah, and Allah says: 'Doer of what He wills' (Hud 11:107). So the acts of obedience are His effects because they are willed by Him. So either they affirm that acts of obedience are created by Him, or they say they are not by His will and thus nullify their own doctrine, or they say that although they are His will, He did not do them, and they deny the text and reject it, and there is that in it.

Then we say: There is no doubt that the goodness of acts of obedience surpasses the goodness of bodies, because their goodness is goodness, and it varies according to the senses, although according to the Mu'tazila there is no way to say that bodies are good because they deny the evil of what is evil among them, even if that is known by sense. So likewise they must deny sense, for it is not known except by what evil is known, and there is no reality for that knowledge, so likewise for this. And the goodness of acts of obedience is rational, and it is something that does not vary according to intellects nor change from state to state. And the superiority of agents is by the superiority of actions, so it would be necessary that every obedient servant be better than Allah, more excellent in action, and higher in rank due to the elevation of his action over Allah's action, and the lowering of the rank of His action over the actions of servants. And in the power of the servant there would be goods that do not resemble or approach that which is in the power of Allah. To say this is a saying the content of which is not hidden. So what is in the power of Allah is Iblis, monkeys, filth, stench, chronic illness, blindness, paralysis, diseases, death, and calamities, and what is in the power of the servant is fasting, prayer, pilgrimage, lending, verification, belief in tawhid, kindness to the needy, charity to them, fulfillment of covenants, discharge of trusts, generosity, and magnanimity, and other virtues that fall under the power of servants. Each one of the agents is empowered according to what is in his power, and he (the servant) takes what he created and wins the best portion and the greatest lot, while the power of the Pre-eternal falls short of that. And because the Mu'tazila know this (as a refutation), they turn away from the side of goods completely and cling to evils so that they might possibly propagate their falsehood upon the weak Muslims. May Allah protect us from that by His generosity and bounty; He is the Possessor of mighty bounty.
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila regarding the divine creation of human actions. The author proceeds as follows:

First, he states that one who understands the proofs previously presented will recognize the truth and not be intimidated by Mu'tazila threats. He will show them that he agrees with some of their premises but reaches different conclusions.

Then, adopting a lenient approach (musāhala), he poses a dilemma: The Mu'tazila deny that Allah creates evil actions because evil cannot be attributed to Allah. But they affirm that good actions (acts of obedience) are by Allah's will. Therefore, consistency demands they affirm that Allah creates these good actions, since there is no obstacle of evil. If they refuse, they are obstinate.

The author strengthens this by citing the Quranic verse 'Doer of what He wills' (Hud 11:107). Since acts of obedience are willed by Allah, they are His effects. The Mu'tazila have three options: (1) admit that Allah creates them, (2) deny they are by His will (which contradicts their own position), or (3) deny the textual evidence.

Next, the author argues that the goodness of acts of obedience is superior to the goodness of physical objects. Goodness of objects is sensory and varies, but the Mu'tazila cannot even affirm sensory goodness because they deny sensory evil. The goodness of obedience is rational and unchanging.

Then comes a reductio ad absurdum: If agents are superior based on the superiority of their actions, then every obedient servant would be better than Allah, since his good deeds are better than what the Mu'tazila claim Allah creates (only evil, filth, etc.). This leads to blasphemous implications: Allah's power would be limited to creating evil and defective things, while the servant's power includes all virtuous deeds. The conclusion is that the Mu'tazila, aware of this devastating objection, avoid discussing good deeds and cling to the discussion of evil to deceive the weak.

The passage ends with a supplication for protection from such deviation.

Misconception: Some may think Nasafi is limiting God's power by listing only evil things in His power; actually he is showing the absurd consequence of the Mu'tazila position.
Correction: Nasafi's list is a rhetorical device to expose the Mu'tazila claim that God only creates evil and not good, which is not his own belief.

Checkpoint
What is the main conclusion of the reductio ad absurdum argument in this passage?
A) The Mu'tazila are correct that God does not create human actions.
B) If the Mu'tazila are right, then every obedient servant would be better than Allah.
C) God's power is limited to creating evil things.
D) The goodness of bodies is superior to the goodness of actions.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi's reductio shows that the Mu'tazila view leads to the blasphemous conclusion that the servant's actions are superior to God's.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that all good actions come from God alone, how does this change the way you view your own acts of worship? Do you feel pride in your obedience, or do you see it as a gift from Allah?
?
When you read the list of evil things that the Mu'tazila attribute to God and the list of good things to the servant, does it disturb you? In what ways might you, even unconsciously, attribute your good deeds to yourself and your bad circumstances to Allah?
?
The Mu'tazila avoid discussing good actions and cling to evils to propagate their falsehood. Are there areas in your life where you focus on what seems negative about God's decree, ignoring the countless blessings? How can you realign your perspective?

Three Reasons for Denying Allah's Creation of Actions
Classification and partial refutation of three reasons for denying takhliq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three categories of reasons that led some groups to deny that Allah creates human actions, and how the author responds to the first two.

Core Idea
Denying Allah's creation stems from ignorance, impossibility, or moral confusion.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi summarizes the core of the debate over human actions. He identifies three distinct motivations behind the denial of Allah's creation (takhliq). By classifying them, he prepares the ground for a systematic refutation. The first two are addressed here, setting up the discussion of the third in subsequent material.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once through, then read the English translation. Notice the structure: the author first lists three reasons in summary, then addresses the first two in order.
The third reason is not refuted in this passage, only mentioned.
2
Identify the three reasons
Look for the three distinct possibilities the author presents: 1) lack of evidence (la dalala), 2) impossibility (ihala), 3) consequences of compulsion (darura) and loss of obligation (taklif).
These are indicated by the phrases 'إما أن يكون ... أو ... أو'.
3
Understand the refutation of the first two
For the first reason (no evidence), the author says he has already provided ample proofs. For the second (impossibility), he demands evidence and states the deniers only have unfounded claims about multiple agents or partnership. Note that he says he has fully discharged responsibility for those points.
This sets up that the real point of contention is the third reason.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومحصول المسألة: أن إنكار تخليقها من الله تعالى، إما أن يكون لما لا دلالة عليها أو للإحالة أو لما في القول به من إيجاب الضرورة وامتناع التكليف وارتفاع الأمر والنهي. فإن كان إنكارهم لعدم الدلالة فقد أقمنا الدلائل السمعية والعقلية ما فيه كفاية لمن نصح نفسه ولم يكابر عقله، وإن كان إنكارهم للإحالة فيطالبون بدليلها، ولا دليل معهم سوى أنه لا يتصور في أوهامهم لكون الشيء عندهم فعلاً لفاعلين وتعلق قدرتين به أو لأن القول به يوجب الشركة، وقد تقصينا عن عهدة كل ذلك.
And the summary of the issue: that denial of His creation of them (actions) from Allah, may He be exalted, is either due to there being no evidence for it, or due to impossibility, or due to what is in holding that of necessitating compulsion and preventing obligation and removing command and prohibition. For if their denial is for lack of evidence, then we have presented auditory and rational proofs sufficient for one who is sincere to himself and does not dispute his intellect. And if their denial is for impossibility, then they are required to provide evidence for it, and there is no evidence with them except that it is not conceivable in their imaginations because a thing, according to them, cannot be an act of two agents and the involvement of two powers with it, or because holding that necessitates partnership. And we have fully discharged responsibility for all of that.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage is a classification and partial refutation. The author begins by summarizing the issue: the denial that Allah creates human actions can arise from three reasons: lack of evidence (no textual or rational proof), impossibility (it is inherently impossible), or because accepting creation would necessitate compulsion (jabr) which would negate moral obligation (taklif). Then he addresses the first two: for the first, he says he has already provided ample scriptural and rational proofs. For the second, he says the deniers have no proof except that they cannot imagine how one act could be attributable to two agents, or that it would imply partnership (shirk) in creating. The author states he has already fully dealt with that.

ضرورة
تكليف

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the Mu'tazila denied Allah's creation for only one reason, such as avoiding compulsion.
Correction: The author shows there are three distinct motivations: lack of evidence, impossibility, and the consequences of compulsion. The third is only mentioned here and is the main point of contention.

Key Takeaway
The denial of Allah's creation of actions can be traced to three distinct rationales, and the first two are shown to be groundless.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Think of a specific sin you committed. Do you truly believe that Allah created that sin, yet holds you accountable? Does that unsettle you? Can you still trust His wisdom and justice even when your mind cannot fully reconcile divine power and human responsibility? What specific act of submission does this require from you today?
?
The author says the impossibility objection is based only on 'what is not conceivable in their imaginations.' When you face a truth that your mind struggles to grasp, do you humble yourself before revelation or cling to your own limited imagination? What belief do you need to surrender to Allah's word rather than your own reasoning?

Free Choice and Creation: The Foundation
Author states necessary knowledge of free will and distinguishes volitional from necessary acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that our knowledge of being free agents is necessary and that creation of actions does not inherently negate free choice.

Core Idea
Free choice is self-evident; creation does not eliminate it.

The author begins by establishing a fundamental point: our awareness of being free agents is a necessary, undeniable knowledge. This is the starting point for the entire discussion. He then immediately addresses the potential conflict: if Allah creates all actions, how can we have free will? The answer lies in distinguishing between types of actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening statement
Read the Arabic passage that begins with 'على أن العلم بكوننا مختارين ثابت بطريق الضرورة'. Notice the claim that our free choice is known necessarily.
This is an epistemological claim about self-awareness.
2
Identify the key distinction
The author asserts that creation does not negate free choice, because there is a difference between volitional (اختياري) and necessary (ضروري) acts. Allah creates volitional acts, not necessary ones.
This distinction is crucial for the argument.
3
Reflect on the opponent's misstep
Ask yourself: why would someone think creation implies compulsion? The author's answer is that they conflate creation with necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على أن العلم بكوننا مختارين ثابت بطريق الضرورة وثبوت الاختيار لا ينفي التخليق لما مر على أن التخليق كيف ينفي الاختيار وهو تعالى يخلق الفعل الاختياري لا الضروري وبينهما مفارقة، والقول بأنه تعالى يريد تخليق أحدهما فيحصل الآخر شاء أو أبى إثبات الاضطرار والعجز للصانع جل وعلا، فكان في جعل الفعل الاختياري ضروريا لحصوله بالتخليق إنكارهم علم الضروريات وجعل الباري مضطرًا في تخليقه، فإن زعموا أن العبد لا يمكنه الخروج عما خلقه فكيف يكون مختارا؟ قلنا : العبد لا يمكنه الخروج عن معلوم الباري، فكيف يكون مختارا والباري لا يخرج أيضا عن معلومه فكيف يكون مختارا؟ وجاء من هذا أنه تعالى لما لم يكن في فعله مضطرًا وإن كان لا يخرج عن معلومه لأنه وإن كان لا يخرج عن معلومه فمعلومه أنه يفعل ما يفعل باختياره فلو صار بعلمه مضطرًا لانقلب جاهلاً حيث علم أنه يفعل ما يفعل باختياره، فلم يفعل بل فعل مضطرًا فكذا عبده لا يصير مضطرًا بعلمه وإن كان لا يخرج عن معلومه لأن معلومه تعالى أن العبد يفعل ما يفعل باختياره غير مضطر ، فلو صار مضطرًا لانقلب علم الباري جهلاً وذلك محال، فبقى العبد مختارا فكذا لما خلق بعلمه الاختياري يبقى مختاراً ؛ إذ لو انقلب بذلك مضطرًا لم يحصل ما خلق على ما خلق بل على غير ما خلق وهو أمارة اضطراره، فكان القول بما قالوا موجبا كون فعل الله تعالى بالاضطرار وهذا محال ، وإذا لم يصر العبد بتخليق فعله مضطرًا في فعله كما لم يصر بتخليق السماوات والأرض فكان خلق كفره وخلق السماوات والأرضين والجبال والبحار سواء من أن لا يوجب اضطرار العبد، والله الموفق.
That the knowledge that we are free agents is established by way of necessity, and the establishment of free choice does not negate creation, as has passed. For how does creation negate free choice? He, exalted, creates the volitional act, not the necessary act, and there is a distinction between them. And the statement that He, exalted, intends to create one of them and the other results whether He wills or not is an affirmation of compulsion and incapacity for the Maker, may He be glorified and exalted. Thus, in making the volitional act necessary due to its occurrence through creation, their denial of the knowledge of necessities and making the Creator compelled in His creation. Then if they claim that the servant cannot exit from what He created for him, so how can he be free? We say: The servant cannot exit from the knowledge of the Creator, so how can he be free? And the Creator also cannot exit from His knowledge, so how can He be free? And it follows from this that He, exalted, is not compelled in His act, even though He cannot exit from His knowledge. For even though He cannot exit from His knowledge, His knowledge is that He does what He does by His choice. For if He became compelled by His knowledge, He would turn ignorant, since He knows that He does what He does by choice; then He did not do it, but rather acted compelled. Similarly, His servant does not become compelled by His knowledge even though he cannot exit from His knowledge, because His knowledge, exalted, is that the servant does what he does by choice, not compelled. For if he became compelled, the knowledge of the Creator would turn into ignorance, and that is impossible. So the servant remains free. Likewise, when He creates his volitional act by His knowledge, he remains free. For if he turned into compelled thereby, what He created would not occur as He created it, but rather in a different way, and that is a sign of his compulsion. Thus, the statement according to what they say necessitates that the act of Allah, exalted, be by compulsion, and this is impossible. And if the servant does not become compelled by the creation of his act, just as he does not become compelled by the creation of the heavens and the earth, then the creation of his disbelief and the creation of the heavens and the earths and mountains and seas are equal in that they do not necessitate the compulsion of the servant. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage is a detailed refutation of the claim that creation of actions implies compulsion. The author begins by asserting that our knowledge of being free agents is necessary. Free choice does not negate creation because there is a distinction between volitional and necessary acts. He then argues that the opponent's position would actually make Allah compelled, which is absurd. Addressing the objection that the servant cannot escape what is created, he uses an analogy: the servant cannot escape Allah's knowledge, but that does not compel him. If creation compelled, then Allah's knowledge (that the servant acts by choice) would be false, which is impossible. Therefore, the servant remains free. He concludes that the opponent's view would force Allah to act by compulsion, which is impossible. Finally, he compares the creation of human actions to the creation of the heavens and earth, which do not compel, so human actions do not compel either.

Key Terms
اختيار
اضطرار
تخليق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If Allah creates all actions, then humans have no free will and are like puppets.
Correction: The author shows that creation does not negate free choice because Allah creates volitional acts, not necessary ones. The act remains freely chosen by the human.

Checkpoint
How does the author describe our knowledge of being free agents?
A) It is acquired through reasoning.
B) It is established by way of necessity.
C) It is a matter of belief.
D) It is derived from revelation.

Key Takeaway
Our free choice is self-evident, and Allah's creation of volitional acts does not remove that freedom.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that your choices are real, or do you sometimes live as if you are a puppet of your circumstances? How does this lesson's affirmation of your free choice challenge the excuses you make for your sins?
?
When you sin, do you feel a genuine sense of responsibility, or do you instinctively blame your nature or environment? How does knowing that Allah creates your volitional acts yet holds you accountable change how you approach repentance?
?
If you were to truly internalize that your free will is self-evident and that Allah Himself distinguishes between volitional and necessary acts, what would you stop delaying in your obedience? What is the first step you will take today to exercise your free will in a way that pleases Allah?

The Analogy of Divine Knowledge
Refutation via analogy: inability to escape knowledge does not imply compulsion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses the analogy of Allah's knowledge to refute the claim that creation compels human actions.

Core Idea
If creation compelled, then Allah's knowledge would be false.

The opponent raises a plausible objection: if the servant cannot escape what Allah creates for him, how can he be free? The author responds with a powerful analogy that turns the argument on its head. He points out that the servant also cannot escape Allah's knowledge, but that does not make him compelled. Similarly, Allah Himself cannot escape His own knowledge, yet He is not compelled.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and the initial answer
Read the Arabic 'فإن زعموا أن العبد لا يمكنه الخروج عما خلقه فكيف يكون مختارا؟ قلنا : العبد لا يمكنه الخروج عن معلوم الباري'. Notice the parallel structure.
2
Analyze the reductio ad absurdum
The author argues that if being unable to escape what is created makes the servant compelled, then being unable to escape Allah's knowledge would also make the servant and even Allah compelled. But that leads to absurdity.
This shows the opponent's logic leads to contradiction.
3
Understand the principle: knowledge does not compel
Allah knows that the servant acts by choice. If the servant were compelled, then Allah's knowledge would be false, which is impossible. Hence the servant remains free.
The argument hinges on the nature of divine knowledge being true.

على أن العلم بكوننا مختارين ثابت بطريق الضرورة وثبوت الاختيار لا ينفي التخليق لما مر على أن التخليق كيف ينفي الاختيار وهو تعالى يخلق الفعل الاختياري لا الضروري وبينهما مفارقة، والقول بأنه تعالى يريد تخليق أحدهما فيحصل الآخر شاء أو أبى إثبات الاضطرار والعجز للصانع جل وعلا، فكان في جعل الفعل الاختياري ضروريا لحصوله بالتخليق إنكارهم علم الضروريات وجعل الباري مضطرًا في تخليقه، فإن زعموا أن العبد لا يمكنه الخروج عما خلقه فكيف يكون مختارا؟ قلنا : العبد لا يمكنه الخروج عن معلوم الباري، فكيف يكون مختارا والباري لا يخرج أيضا عن معلومه فكيف يكون مختارا؟ وجاء من هذا أنه تعالى لما لم يكن في فعله مضطرًا وإن كان لا يخرج عن معلومه لأنه وإن كان لا يخرج عن معلومه فمعلومه أنه يفعل ما يفعل باختياره فلو صار بعلمه مضطرًا لانقلب جاهلاً حيث علم أنه يفعل ما يفعل باختياره، فلم يفعل بل فعل مضطرًا فكذا عبده لا يصير مضطرًا بعلمه وإن كان لا يخرج عن معلومه لأن معلومه تعالى أن العبد يفعل ما يفعل باختياره غير مضطر ، فلو صار مضطرًا لانقلب علم الباري جهلاً وذلك محال، فبقى العبد مختارا فكذا لما خلق بعلمه الاختياري يبقى مختاراً ؛ إذ لو انقلب بذلك مضطرًا لم يحصل ما خلق على ما خلق بل على غير ما خلق وهو أمارة اضطراره، فكان القول بما قالوا موجبا كون فعل الله تعالى بالاضطرار وهذا محال ، وإذا لم يصر العبد بتخليق فعله مضطرًا في فعله كما لم يصر بتخليق السماوات والأرض فكان خلق كفره وخلق السماوات والأرضين والجبال والبحار سواء من أن لا يوجب اضطرار العبد، والله الموفق.
That the knowledge that we are free agents is established by way of necessity, and the establishment of free choice does not negate creation, as has passed. For how does creation negate free choice? He, exalted, creates the volitional act, not the necessary act, and there is a distinction between them. And the statement that He, exalted, intends to create one of them and the other results whether He wills or not is an affirmation of compulsion and incapacity for the Maker, may He be glorified and exalted. Thus, in making the volitional act necessary due to its occurrence through creation, their denial of the knowledge of necessities and making the Creator compelled in His creation. Then if they claim that the servant cannot exit from what He created for him, so how can he be free? We say: The servant cannot exit from the knowledge of the Creator, so how can he be free? And the Creator also cannot exit from His knowledge, so how can He be free? And it follows from this that He, exalted, is not compelled in His act, even though He cannot exit from His knowledge. For even though He cannot exit from His knowledge, His knowledge is that He does what He does by His choice. For if He became compelled by His knowledge, He would turn ignorant, since He knows that He does what He does by choice; then He did not do it, but rather acted compelled. Similarly, His servant does not become compelled by His knowledge even though he cannot exit from His knowledge, because His knowledge, exalted, is that the servant does what he does by choice, not compelled. For if he became compelled, the knowledge of the Creator would turn into ignorance, and that is impossible. So the servant remains free. Likewise, when He creates his volitional act by His knowledge, he remains free. For if he turned into compelled thereby, what He created would not occur as He created it, but rather in a different way, and that is a sign of his compulsion. Thus, the statement according to what they say necessitates that the act of Allah, exalted, be by compulsion, and this is impossible. And if the servant does not become compelled by the creation of his act, just as he does not become compelled by the creation of the heavens and the earth, then the creation of his disbelief and the creation of the heavens and the earths and mountains and seas are equal in that they do not necessitate the compulsion of the servant. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage is a detailed refutation of the claim that creation of actions implies compulsion. The author begins by asserting that our knowledge of being free agents is necessary. Free choice does not negate creation because there is a distinction between volitional and necessary acts. He then argues that the opponent's position would actually make Allah compelled, which is absurd. Addressing the objection that the servant cannot escape what is created, he uses an analogy: the servant cannot escape Allah's knowledge, but that does not compel him. If creation compelled, then Allah's knowledge (that the servant acts by choice) would be false, which is impossible. Therefore, the servant remains free. He concludes that the opponent's view would force Allah to act by compulsion, which is impossible. Finally, he compares the creation of human actions to the creation of the heavens and earth, which do not compel, so human actions do not compel either.

Key Terms
معلوم
اختيار
اضطرار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If Allah knows what we will do, then we are forced to do it.
Correction: Knowledge is not causative. Allah knows our free choices, but that knowledge does not compel us; it simply reflects what we will freely choose.

Checkpoint
What absurdity does the author point out if the servant becomes compelled by creation?
A) The servant would be equal to Allah.
B) Allah's knowledge would become ignorance.
C) The act would be uncreated.
D) The heavens would fall.

Key Takeaway
Divine knowledge of our actions does not compel us; if it did, Allah's own knowledge of His actions would compel Him, which is absurd.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you ever say to yourself, 'It was written for me' as an excuse? How does this passage challenge that excuse? What would you say to Allah on the Day of Judgment if you used that excuse?
?
If Allah's knowledge of your actions does not compel you, then what is truly preventing you from obeying Him? What is the real obstacle in your heart?
?
This passage says that if Allah were compelled by His knowledge, He would be ignorant. In what areas of your life do you act as if Allah's knowledge compels you? What would change if you truly believed you are free?

Divine Decree
intermediate
6 min
Creation Does Not Compel: Final Argument
Final argument: creation of act does not compel, as shown by creation of heavens/earth; opponent's view implies compulsion for Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's final argument that the creation of human actions does not compel the servant, using the analogy of the creation of the heavens and earth.

Core Idea
Creation of actions is like creation of the universe — it does not force.

Having established that creation does not negate free choice, the author concludes with a striking comparison. He argues that if creation of an act implied compulsion, then the creation of the heavens and earth would also compel, which is clearly not the case. Therefore, the creation of human actions, including disbelief, does not force the servant. The opponent's position ultimately leads to attributing compulsion to Allah, which is impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the concluding passage
Read the Arabic from 'فكذا لما خلق بعلمه الاختياري يبقى مختاراً' to the end. Notice how the author wraps up the argument.
2
Understand the comparison with natural creation
The author points out that just as the creation of the heavens and earth does not compel the servant, the creation of his actions does not compel him either.
This shows consistency in Allah's creative act.
3
See the absurdity of the opponent's view
If the opponent's logic were correct, then Allah would be acting under compulsion in creating, which is impossible.
The opponent's position is self-contradictory.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على أن العلم بكوننا مختارين ثابت بطريق الضرورة وثبوت الاختيار لا ينفي التخليق لما مر على أن التخليق كيف ينفي الاختيار وهو تعالى يخلق الفعل الاختياري لا الضروري وبينهما مفارقة، والقول بأنه تعالى يريد تخليق أحدهما فيحصل الآخر شاء أو أبى إثبات الاضطرار والعجز للصانع جل وعلا، فكان في جعل الفعل الاختياري ضروريا لحصوله بالتخليق إنكارهم علم الضروريات وجعل الباري مضطرًا في تخليقه، فإن زعموا أن العبد لا يمكنه الخروج عما خلقه فكيف يكون مختارا؟ قلنا : العبد لا يمكنه الخروج عن معلوم الباري، فكيف يكون مختارا والباري لا يخرج أيضا عن معلومه فكيف يكون مختارا؟ وجاء من هذا أنه تعالى لما لم يكن في فعله مضطرًا وإن كان لا يخرج عن معلومه لأنه وإن كان لا يخرج عن معلومه فمعلومه أنه يفعل ما يفعل باختياره فلو صار بعلمه مضطرًا لانقلب جاهلاً حيث علم أنه يفعل ما يفعل باختياره، فلم يفعل بل فعل مضطرًا فكذا عبده لا يصير مضطرًا بعلمه وإن كان لا يخرج عن معلومه لأن معلومه تعالى أن العبد يفعل ما يفعل باختياره غير مضطر ، فلو صار مضطرًا لانقلب علم الباري جهلاً وذلك محال، فبقى العبد مختارا فكذا لما خلق بعلمه الاختياري يبقى مختاراً ؛ إذ لو انقلب بذلك مضطرًا لم يحصل ما خلق على ما خلق بل على غير ما خلق وهو أمارة اضطراره، فكان القول بما قالوا موجبا كون فعل الله تعالى بالاضطرار وهذا محال ، وإذا لم يصر العبد بتخليق فعله مضطرًا في فعله كما لم يصر بتخليق السماوات والأرض فكان خلق كفره وخلق السماوات والأرضين والجبال والبحار سواء من أن لا يوجب اضطرار العبد، والله الموفق.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah creates all your actions, do you truly feel responsible for your sins? How does this passage change that feeling, if at all?
?

?
Consider one area of your life where you feel spiritually stuck. How might the truth that creation does not compel break that stuckness and move you to sincere action?

Abu Hashim's Objection on Compulsion (Incomplete)
Abu Hashim's objection linking creation to compulsion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Abu Hashim's objection that the servant's inability to exit from Allah's creation implies compulsion, and why this argument is incomplete without the author's response.

Core Idea
Can't escape created actions? Objection says compulsion.

This lesson presents an objection raised by Abu Hashim against the view that humans are free agents. He argues that because a person cannot avoid what Allah has created—such as motion or its opposite—they are compelled. The passage is cut off, so the response is not preserved here, but understanding the objection is crucial for grasping the broader debate on human action and divine creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that it is a single sentence cut off at the end. Focus on the logical structure: premise (cannot exit from creation) leads to conclusion (compulsion).
The text ends with 'فكان' indicating the argument is incomplete.
2
Identify the core argument
Abu Hashim's objection: The servant cannot exit from what Allah has created (e.g., motion and its opposite). Therefore, the servant is compelled. Ask yourself: Is this inference valid? Does inability to avoid created things mean total compulsion?
3
Consider the missing response
Since the text is truncated, think about what a Maturidi theologian might reply. From previous lessons, recall that inability to exit from creation does not negate moral responsibility; the servant still acquires actions and is accountable for choices made within that framework.
The full response is not in this passage, but the broader context provides a refutation.
4
Reflect on the misunderstanding
One might think this objection disproves free will. However, the objection itself is incomplete and the intended response would clarify that being under Allah's creation does not entail compulsion in the sense of coercion without choice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و عورض أبو هاشم في قوله : إن العبد لما لم يمكنه الخروج عن مخلوق الله تعالى كان مضطرًا إذ العبد لا يمكنه الخروج عن الحركة وضدها، فكان
And Abu Hashim was objected to in his statement: Since the servant cannot exit from what Allah has created, he is compelled, for the servant cannot exit from motion and its opposite, so it was
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage presents an objection attributed to Abu Hashim. The objection states that because the servant cannot exit from what Allah has created for him, he must be compelled. The author adds that the servant cannot exit from motion and its opposite. The text is cut off, so the response is not fully presented. However, from the previous arguments, one can infer that the author would reply that inability to exit from creation does not imply compulsion any more than inability to exit from Allah's knowledge implies compulsion.

Key Terms
اضطرار
مخلوق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The objection proves that humans are completely compelled and have no free will.
Correction: The objection is incomplete; the author would argue that inability to escape creation does not negate moral responsibility, as the servant still makes choices within that framework.

Checkpoint
What is the conclusion that Abu Hashim draws from the premise that the servant cannot exit from what Allah has created?
A) The servant is free.
B) The servant is compelled.
C) The servant is unable to act.
D) The servant is independent.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hashim's objection linking creation to compulsion is presented but not fully answered in this passage; the broader Maturidi position offers a nuanced response preserving human responsibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you disobey Allah, do you ever catch yourself thinking, 'I couldn't help it, Allah created my circumstances'? How does Abu Hashim's objection—that inability to exit from creation implies compulsion—either reveal or conceal your own heart's evasions? This week, whenever you are tempted to blame your environment, pause and ask: Am I denying my own role by invoking Allah's decree?
?
If the Maturidi response to this objection is that creation does not negate acquisition, what does that mean for the sins you committed yesterday? Can you honestly accept that you are fully responsible, even though Allah created all things? Spend time in solitude asking yourself: Am I ready to stand before Allah without shifting the blame to Him?
